Mu'tazila Divisions on Intercession
Baqillani reports the Mu'tazila's division on intercession and their three categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two Mu'tazila positions on intercession and the three categories of believers for whom intercession is affirmed by one group.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila split over intercession: one group denies it entirely, the other restricts it to three types of believers.

Imam Baqillani now turns to the Mu'tazila's views on intercession, a key topic in eschatology (sam'iyyat). He reports that they divided into two factions: one completely rejecting intercession, and another affirming it but only for specific categories of believers. This passage clarifies the latter's criteria, setting the stage for his refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice the two-part structure: first the denial group, then the affirmation group with its three categories.
The affirmation group's list is crucial.
2
Identify the two Mu'tazila groups
Note the two groups: one denies intercession entirely, the other affirms it for three categories. Understand why the first group is criticised for rejecting reports and the Qur'an.
3
Examine the three categories
List the three categories: (1) those with minor sins avoiding major, (2) repentant major sinners, (3) sinless believers. Understand that intercession is for increase in reward, not forgiveness.
Pay attention to the exclusion: intercession is invalid for unrepentant major sinners.
4
Ask: why does this matter?
Reflect on how this Mu'tazila view limits intercession compared to the Sunni belief. This passage sets up the contrast Baqillani will refute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل وقد افترقت المعتزلة فريقين. فأنكر فريق منهم الشفاعة جملة وحمل نفسه على جحد الأخبار ورد القرآن. وقال الفريق الآخر إن للأنبياء والملائكة شفاعة، إلا أنها تشفع لثلاثة فرق من الناس المؤمنين. ففريق من أهل الشفاعة هم أصحاب الصغائر الذين واقعوها مع مجانبة الكبائر. والفريق الآخر أصحاب الكبائر الذين تابوا منها وندموا عليها. والفريق الآخر هم المؤمنون الذين لا ذنب لهم أصلاً. فتكون شفاعة الأنبياء والملائكة فيهم شفاعة في الزيادة لهم من النعيم على قدر ما يستحقون بأعمالهم. فأما الشفاعة في صاحب كبيرة إذا مات مصراً عليها فإنها باطلة.
Chapter: The Mu'tazila have split into two groups. One group denied intercession entirely and forced themselves to reject the reports and the Qur'an. The other group said that the prophets and angels have intercession, but it intercedes for three groups of believing people: a group among the people of intercession are the people of minor sins who commit them while avoiding major sins; the other group are the people of major sins who repented from them and regretted them; and the other group are the believers who have no sin at all. So the intercession of the prophets and angels for them is intercession for increase in bliss commensurate with what they deserve by their deeds. As for intercession for a person of a major sin, if he dies persisting in it, it is invalid.
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage classifies the Mu'tazila positions on intercession. Baqillani first notes that the Mu'tazila split into two factions: one completely denies intercession, while the other affirms it for three categories of believers. These categories are: (1) those who commit minor sins while avoiding major ones, (2) those who committed major sins but repented, and (3) sinless believers. For the first two groups, the intercession is not for forgiveness but for increase in reward. However, for a major sinner who dies unrepentant, intercession is invalid. This sets up the subsequent refutation.

Key Terms
شفاعة (intercession)
صغائر (minor sins)
كبائر (major sins)
توبة (repentance)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All Mu'tazila deny intercession.
Correction: Only one group denied it; another affirmed it for three categories of believers.

Checkpoint
According to the Mu'tazila group that affirms intercession, for whom is intercession invalid?
A) Those with minor sins
B) Those who repented from major sins
C) Those with no sins
D) A major sinner who dies unrepentant

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila who affirm intercession restrict it to minor sinners, repentant major sinners, and the sinless, denying it for unrepentant major sinners.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If intercession is only for increase in reward and not for forgiveness, where does that leave your hope for the Prophet's intercession on your behalf? Will you continue to rely on it without striving to avoid major sins?
?
The Mu'tazila who affirmed intercession restricted it to those who are already righteous or repentant. Does your current state of obedience give you confidence that you would be among those three categories, or are you delaying repentance and hoping for intercession to cover your persistence?
?
When you hear that intercession is invalid for the unrepentant major sinner, how does that challenge your assumptions about Allah's mercy? Are you willing to change something today to ensure you do not die persisting in a major sin?

Intercession for the First Two Groups Is Pointless
Baqillani argues that intercession for minor sinners and repentant major sinners is pointless.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Baqillani argues that intercession for minor sinners and repentant major sinners is meaningless based on the Mu'tazila's own principles.

Core Idea
Intercession for those who don't need it is meaningless.

Baqillani continues his refutation of the Mu'tazila claim about intercession. In this passage, he addresses the first two of their four groups: minor sinners and repentant major sinners. He argues that these groups do not need intercession because, according to Mu'tazila principles, they are not deserving of punishment or have already removed it. Thus, the concept of intercession for them becomes incoherent.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Baqillani uses a very direct refutation style.
2
Identify the two groups
The passage mentions two groups: those who commit minor sins while avoiding major sins, and those who repent from major sins. Identify each and note how Baqillani describes their status according to Mu'tazila principles.
3
Understand why intercession is meaningless
Baqillani argues that intercession for these groups would be intercession to God not to be unjust. Since the first group does not deserve punishment and the second has already removed it through repentance, such intercession is unnecessary. Ask yourself: why does this refute the Mu'tazila position?
This connects to the learning objective.
4
Reflect on the argument's force
Consider how Baqillani uses the Mu'tazila's own principles against them. If they believe minor sinners are not punished when avoiding major sins, and repentance removes punishment, then intercession becomes meaningless. This shows an inconsistency in their claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيقال لهم : أما الشفاعة للفريقين الأولين فلا معنى لها. لأنها شفاعة إلى الله في أن لا يظلم ولا يجور على عباده بعقاب غير مستحق. لأن صاحب الصغيرة غير مستحق للعذاب إذا فعلها مع مجانبة الكبائر عندكم وعلى أصولكم. وكذلك التائب من الكبيرة قد أزال عن نفسه العقاب بتوبته وصار عقابه عليها مع التوبة ظلماً قبيحاً. فلا معنى للشفاعة فيمن هذه حاله.
It is said to them: As for intercession for the first two groups, it has no meaning. Because it is intercession to God that He not be unjust nor tyrannical to His servants with undeserved punishment. Because the person of a minor sin does not deserve punishment when he commits it while avoiding major sins according to you and your principles. Likewise, the repentant from a major sin has removed punishment from himself by his repentance, and his punishment upon it with repentance would be base injustice. So there is no meaning for intercession for one whose state is this.
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage refutes the Mu'tazila claim of intercession for the first two categories. Baqillani argues that intercession is meaningless because the first group (minor sinners) does not deserve punishment according to Mu'tazila principles, and the second group (repentant major sinners) has already removed punishment through repentance. Thus, intercession would be for God not to be unjust, which is an inherent attribute of God, not something needing intercession. The Mu'tazila's own principles render their position inconsistent.

Key Terms
ظلم (injustice)
عقاب غير مستحق (undeserved punishment)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That intercession is needed for all sinners regardless of their state.
Correction: Baqillani shows that according to Mu'tazila own principles, minor sinners and repentant major sinners do not need intercession, making the claim inconsistent.

Checkpoint
Why does Baqillani say intercession for the first two groups is meaningless?
A) Because they are not believers
B) Because they do not desire intercession
C) Because they do not deserve punishment or have already repented
D) Because the prophets refuse to intercede

Key Takeaway
Baqillani demonstrates that the Mu'tazila's own principles make intercession for the first two groups meaningless.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever secretly hoped that someone else's intercession might cover sins you are not truly repentant of? How does Baqillani's argument expose that hope as relying on God being potentially unjust? What will you actually change today in your repentance so that you don't need such a loophole?
?
If you truly believe that repentance removes punishment, why do you still fear God's justice for past sins while not actively repenting with full sincerity? This lesson forces you to confront whether your hope for intercession masks a lack of genuine tawba. What is one sin you will repent from right now, making it completely between you and Allah, without expecting any shortcut?

The Real Subject of Debate: Intercession in Revelation
Baqillani clarifies the true subject of the debate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Muslim community's debate about intercession centers on the reality of the intercession attested in the Qur'an and hadith, not on the possibility of increasing reward.

Core Idea
Intercession is about revelation, not reward increase.

Baqillani now refocuses the debate. He states clearly that the discussion among Muslims is not about whether reward can be increased, but about the intercession that is mentioned in the Qur'an and the prophetic reports. He challenges the Mu'tazila to either affirm its meaning or face the consequence of rejecting revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the structure: a statement of what the debate is NOT, then what it IS, then a challenge.
2
Identify the core claim
Baqillani says the real issue is the intercession that came in the reports and the Qur'an. Why does he emphasize this?
He is shifting from theoretical possibility to textual evidence.
3
Consider the consequence
If the Mu'tazila deny intercession, they fall into rejecting the Qur'an and narrations. What does this imply about their position?
This is a strong reductio ad absurdum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقال لهم : ليس الكلام بين الأمة في الزيادة على قدر الثواب وإنما الكلام في الشفاعة التي جاءت بها الأخبار والقرآن فهل لها عندكم معنى أم لا؟ فإن قالوا: لا صاروا إلى جحد القرآن والروايات، وسألناهم على حد ما تقدم.
And it is said to them: The discussion among the community is not about increase beyond the amount of reward; rather the discussion is about the intercession that came in the reports and the Qur'an. So does it have any meaning according to you or not? If they say: No, they fall into rejection of the Qur'an and the narrations, and we will question them as previously mentioned.
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This concluding passage refocuses the debate. Baqillani states that the real issue is whether the intercession attested in the Qur'an and hadith has any reality. If the Mu'tazila deny it, they are rejecting revelation. The earlier arguments showed that their alternative interpretations are self-referentially incoherent.

Key Terms
زيادة الثواب (increase of reward)
جحد القرآن (denial of the Qur'an)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The debate is about whether Allah can increase reward beyond what is deserved.
Correction: Baqillani clarifies that the debate is about the reality of intercession as reported in revelation.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what is the real subject of the debate?
A) Whether reward can be increased
B) Whether intercession in the Qur'an and hadith has meaning
C) Whether prophets can sin
D) Whether angels exist

Key Takeaway
The debate about intercession hinges on accepting the reality of what revelation reports, not on speculative possibilities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a teaching from the Qur'an or hadith that seems difficult to accept (like intercession), do you find yourself reinterpreting it away or dismissing it because it doesn't fit your reasoning? Read the passage again: Baqillani says denying it amounts to rejecting the Qur'an and narrations. How does this challenge your approach to difficult texts?
?
The Mu'tazila denied intercession because they thought it conflicted with justice. Is there any aspect of your faith that you have doubted or reinterpreted because it didn't align with your sense of fairness? What would it mean for you to submit to revelation even when it challenges your own reasoning?
?
Baqillani forces a binary: either accept intercession as it appears in the revelation or fall into rejection. Have you ever been in a situation where you had to choose between what your intellect says and what the text says? How did you decide?

Three Objections Against the Imamate and Their Refutations
Baqillani presents three objections and answers the first two.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three common objections raised against the necessity of appointing an imam and Baqillani's responses, including his argument for the practical necessity of coercive authority.

Core Idea
Practical necessity of coercive authority to prevent societal chaos.

In this passage, Baqillani addresses three objections from those who deny the need for an imam. The first objection argues that people naturally manage their affairs; the second claims benefit only through direct access; the third points to unrealistic conditions. Baqillani refutes the first two with empirical observations and logical points, while the third answer remains incomplete in the text. Let's examine his arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the objections
Familiarize yourself with the three objections presented by the opponent. Note how each challenges the necessity of an imam.
The objections are: sufficiency of human nature, impracticality of direct access, and stringent conditions.
2
Analyze answer to first objection
Baqillani shifts from theoretical possibility to practical impossibility, using historical examples of chaos at the death of governors and the behavior of bedouins. He quotes proverbs to emphasize the role of coercive authority.
The proverbs: 'The sultan restrains more than the Qur'an' and 'Sword and spear do what proof does not do.'
3
Examine answer to second objection
Baqillani rejects the premise that benefit requires direct physical access. Instead, benefit comes through the imam's rulings reaching the subjects.
This redefines the function of the imam as a source of law rather than a personal intervener.
4
Consider the third objection
The third objection and the beginning of Baqillani's answer are present, but the answer is cut off. Reflect on what a complete refutation might entail.
The text ends at 'بل بوصول أحكامه'? Actually, the arabic continues but the answer is missing after that? Check source: the arabic ends after 'وعن الثاني: لا نسلم...' but the third objection and answer are not fully given? The arabic_clean includes the third objection as part of the passage, but the commentary says the answer is incomplete. Actually, the arabic_clean includes: 'الثالث: للإمامة شروط...' and then the answer to first and second, but no answer to third. So the third objection is stated but not answered. So in the source_arabic we include the full arabic_clean as given. Then in commentary note that the answer to the third is not provided.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
احتج المانع بوجوده. الأول: توفر الناس على مصالحهم مما يحث عليه طباعهم وأديانهم فلا حاجة إلى نصب من يتحكم عليهم فيما يستقلون به ويدل عليه انتظام أحوال العربان والبوادي الخارجين عن حكم السلطان. الثاني: الانتفاع بالإمام إنما يكون بالوصول إليه ولا يخفى تعذر وصول آحاد الرعية إليه في كل ما يعن لهم من الأمور الدنيوية عادة. الثالث: للإمامة شروط قلما توجد في كل عصر فإن أقاموا فاقدها لم يأتوا بالواجب، وإن لم يقيموه فقد تركوا الواجب. فالجواب عن الأول: أنه وإن كان ممكناً عقلاً فممتنع عادة لما يرى من توازن الفتن والاختلافات عند موت الولاة، ولذلك صادفنا العربان والبوادي كالذئاب الشاردة والأسود الضارية لا يبقى بعضهم على بعض ولا يحافظ في الغالب على سنة ولا فرض وليس تشوفهم إلى العمل بموجب دينهم غالباً، ولذلك قيل: ما يزع السلطان أكثر مما يزع القرآن، وقيل: السيف والسنان يفعلان ما لا يفعل البرهان. وعن الثاني: لا نسلم أن الانتفاع بالإمام إنما يكون بالوصول إليه، بل بوصول أحكامه.
The opponent argued against its existence. First: People are sufficient for their interests by what their natures and religions urge them to, so there is no need to appoint someone to dominate them in what they manage independently. This is indicated by the orderly condition of the bedouins and villagers outside the ruler's authority. Second: Benefit from the imam is only through access to him, and it is not hidden that access of individual subjects to him is impossible in every worldly matter that concerns them customarily. Third: Imamate has conditions rarely found in every age. If they appoint someone lacking them, they have not fulfilled the obligation; if they do not appoint him, they have neglected the obligation. The answer to the first: That although it is possible in reason, it is impossible customarily, because of what is seen of the succession of tribulations and disagreements at the death of governors. For that reason we find the bedouins and villagers like stray wolves and ravenous lions: they do not spare one another, and generally they do not preserve a sunna or an obligation, and they are not eager to act according to their religion most of the time. Hence it is said: 'The sultan restrains more than the Qur'an restrains.' And it is said: 'The sword and the spear do what proof does not do.' And regarding the second: We do not grant that benefit from the imam is only through access to him; rather it is through the access of his rulings.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage presents three objections from the opponent (al-mani') against the necessity of appointing an imam, along with Baqillani's replies. The first objection is that people naturally pursue their own interests, so no external ruler is needed; this is seen in the self-sufficient order of bedouin tribes outside state control. Baqillani answers that while this is theoretically possible, it is practically impossible given historical observations: whenever governors die, fitnah and disagreement erupt, showing that bedouins behave like wild animals who observe no religious law. He quotes proverbs: 'The sultan restrains more than the Qur'an' and 'Sword and spear do what proof does not do,' emphasizing the practical necessity of coercive authority. The second objection is that benefit from an imam requires direct access, which is unrealistic for all subjects in all their daily matters. Baqillani rejects this premise: benefit comes not necessarily through physical access but through the imam's rulings reaching them. The third objection states that conditions for a valid imam are so stringent that no one qualifies; if an unqualified person is appointed, the obligation is violated, and if no one is appointed, the obligation is also violated. The text ends at page 436, and the answer to the third objection seems to be incomplete (perhaps continued on a later page).

Key Terms
المانع
العربان
السلطان
شروط الإمامة
الوصول إلى الإمام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Human natural inclination and religion alone are sufficient to maintain social order without a ruler.
Correction: Baqillani argues that empirical evidence shows that when authority is absent, chaos ensues, as seen in bedouin tribes and at the death of governors.

Checkpoint
How does Baqillani refute the objection that benefit from an imam requires direct access?
A) By arguing that access is possible
B) By stating that benefit comes through the imam's rulings
C) By saying the objection is irrelevant
D) By quoting a hadith

Key Takeaway
Baqillani defends the necessity of an imam by showing that human nature and religion do not prevent conflict; coercive authority is practically indispensable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If all rulers and authorities were removed tomorrow, would your commitment to Islamic law remain strong without any external enforcement? What does your honest answer reveal about your own faith?
?
Think of a time you followed a religious command only because you feared punishment from an authority. Would you have obeyed out of mere devotion? What does that say about human nature?
?
The passage states that 'the sultan restrains more than the Qur'an.' Does this reality trouble you? Are you willing to admit that coercion plays a role in your own religious practice, and if so, how does that change your reliance on Allah versus reliance on power?

Refutation of Nass: Why Election Is the Valid Path
Baqillani argues for election and refutes explicit designation via transmission argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's argument that the absence of widespread transmission of a designation proves the invalidity of nass and establishes election as the way to choose the imam.

Core Idea
If the Prophet had designated a successor, all would have known.

In this passage, Imam al-Baqillani tackles a foundational difference between Sunni and Shia theology: how is the imam chosen? The Shia claim the Prophet explicitly named a successor (nass), while Sunnis hold that the community elects. Baqillani presents a simple but powerful argument: if such a designation had occurred, it would have been transmitted as widely as the pillars of Islam. Its absence in tradition is the clearest proof of its falsehood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the full English translation. Let the argument's flow settle in your mind.
The passage is a direct question-and-answer format.
2
Identify the two methods for imamate
Notice that Baqillani says there are only two ways: nass (explicit designation) and ikhtiyar (election). He then sets out to prove nass is invalid, leaving ikhtiyar as the only valid path.
This is a classic either/or argument.
3
Follow the transmission argument
Baqillani asks: If the Prophet had designated a successor, would that announcement have been public? He argues it would have been transmitted like other major obligations. Since we have no such widely transmitted report, nass must be invalid.
Notice the analogy with prayer, Hajj, and fasting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الكلام في إبطال النص وتصحيح الاختيار. إن سأل سائل فقال : ما الدليل على ما تذهبون إليه من الاختيار للأمة وإبطال النص على إمام بعينه؟ قيل له : الدليل على هذا أنه إذا فسد النص صح الاختيار لأن الأمة متفقة على أنه ليس طريق إثبات الإمامة إلا هذين الطريقين ومتى فسد أحدهما صح الآخر والذي يدل على إبطال النص أنه لو نص النبي صلّى الله عليه وسلم على إمام بعينه وفرض طاعته على الأمة دون غيره وقال لهم : هذا خليفتي والإمام من بعدي فاسمعوا له وأطيعوا، لكان لا يخلو أن يكون قال ذلك وفرضه بمحضر من الصحابة أو الجمهور منهم بحضرة الواحد والاثنين ومن لا يوجب خبره العلم فإن كان قد أعلن ذلك وأظهره وقاله قولاً ذائعاً فيهم وجب أن ينقل ذلك نقل مثله مما شاع وذاع من نحو الصلوات وفرض الحج والصيام وغيرهما من العبادات التي لا اختلاف بين الأمة في أنها مشروعة مفروضة في دين النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ولا سيما إن كان فرض الإمامة من الفرائض العامة اللازمة لكل أحد في عينه وكان النص من النبي صلّى الله عليه وسلم أمراً عظيماً وخطراً جسيماً لا ينكتم مثله ولا يستتر عن الناس علمه مع العلم بأن الأمة قد نقلت بأسرها تولية النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم الإمرة لزيد بن حارثة ولأسامة بن زيد بن زيد وعبد الله بن
Chapter on refuting designation and confirming election. If a questioner asks: What is the proof for your position of election for the community and refutation of designation upon a specific imam? It is said to him: The proof for this is that if designation is invalid, then election is valid, because the community agrees that there is no way to establish the imamate except these two ways, and when one of them is invalid, the other becomes valid. And what indicates the invalidity of designation is that if the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, had designated a specific imam and prescribed obedience to him for the community to the exclusion of others, and said to them: 'This is my caliph and the imam after me, so hear and obey him', it would not be free from either that he said that and prescribed it in the presence of the Companions or the majority of them, or in the presence of one or two or those whose report does not necessitate knowledge. If he had announced it and made it public and said it as a widespread saying among them, then it would have been transmitted like the transmission of similar widespread matters such as the prayers, the obligation of Hajj and fasting, and other acts of worship about which there is no disagreement among the community that they are legislated and obligatory in the religion of the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace. Especially since the obligation of the imamate is among the general obligations binding on every individual, and the designation from the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, would be a great matter and a grave affair, the like of which cannot be concealed nor hidden from people's knowledge, especially since the community as a whole has transmitted the appointment of the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, of Zayd ibn Haritha and Usama ibn Zayd and Abdullah ibn...
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the Sunni position that the imam is chosen by election (ikhtiyar) of the community, and a refutation of the Shia claim of explicit designation (nass) by the Prophet of a specific person. Baqillani begins with a question asking for evidence. The answer presents a two-step argument: First, the only ways to establish the imamate are nass and ikhtiyar; if nass is invalid, ikhtiyar is valid. Second, to prove the invalidity of nass, he argues that if the Prophet had designated someone, it would have been a public announcement, and it would have been transmitted widely, just like the obligations of prayer, Hajj, and fasting. But in fact, there is no such widespread transmission. Moreover, even lesser appointments like those of Zayd and Usama were transmitted, so a major one like imamate would certainly be transmitted. Since it is not, nass is invalid. The argument is a classic Sunni proof against the Shia doctrine of nass.

Key Terms
نَصّ
اِخْتِيَار
إِمَامَة
صَحَابَة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Shia claim that the Prophet secretly designated Ali as his successor, and that this designation was known only to a few.
Correction: Baqillani argues that a matter of such gravity would necessarily have been public and transmitted widely. The absence of such transmission disproves the claim.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, why is the claim of explicit designation (nass) of an imam invalid?
A) Because the Prophet never mentioned the imamate
B) Because if it had occurred it would have been transmitted widely like other obligations
C) Because the community rejected it
D) Because the imamate is not obligatory

Key Takeaway
The absence of widespread transmission of a prophetic designation proves that no explicit designation occurred, leaving election as the only valid method for choosing the imam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Prophet had publicly designated a leader, you would be obligated to follow without question. Since he did not, the choice of leaders is your collective responsibility. Who are you following today—a leader chosen by the community or one claimed by private designation—and have you verified their legitimacy against this proof?
?
Baqillani argues that important matters are always widely transmitted. Think of the most important truth you hold about God or the Prophet. How was it transmitted to you? Are you as certain of it as the early Muslims were of prayer and Hajj? If not, what does that say about your faith?
?
The absence of a report is itself evidence in this argument. Is there a duty or command from God that you ignore because it is not 'loud enough' in your life? Will you wait for a clear public designation before obeying, or will you take responsibility to seek and follow the truth now?

Refuting Nass: Why Explicit Designation Was Not Transmitted
Baqillani argues that absence of transmission proves no nass.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's argument that the absence of widespread transmission of an explicit designation proves that no such designation occurred, thus supporting the Sunni doctrine of election.

Core Idea
If the Prophet had designated an Imam, it would be as famous as prayer.

This passage tackles a central disagreement with the Shia: whether the Prophet explicitly designated a successor. Baqillani presents a historical-argumentative proof: if such a designation had occurred, it would have been transmitted as widely as the five pillars. Since it was not, election is the only valid method.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Notice how Baqillani sets up the question and then argues step by step.
The passage ends mid-sentence; focus on the complete argument up to that point.
2
Identify the two ways to establish Imamate
Baqillani states that the community agrees there are only two methods: explicit designation (nass) and election (ikhtiyar). Understand that if one is invalid, the other must be valid.
3
Trace the conditional argument
Follow Baqillani's logic: if the Prophet had publicly designated an Imam, it would have been transmitted like other obligations. Since it was not transmitted, the claim is false. Compare with known appointments of commanders.
This is a reductio ad absurdum argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الكلام في إبطال النص وتصحيح الاختيار

إن سأل سائل فقال: ما الدليل على ما تذهبون إليه من الاختيار للأمة وإبطال النص على إمام بعينه؟ قيل له: الدليل على هذا أنه إذا فسد النص من الطريقين ومتى فسد أحدهما صح الاختيار لأن الأمة متفقة على أنه ليس طريق إثبات الإمامة إلا هذين. والذي يدل على إبطال النص أنه لو نص النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم على إمام بعينه وفرض طاعته على الأمة دون غيره وقال لهم: هذا خليفتي والإمام من بعدي فاسمعوا له وأطيعوا، لكان لا يخلو أن يكون قال ذلك وفرضه بمحضر من الصحابة أو الجمهور منهم بحضرة الواحد والاثنين ومن لا يوجب خبره العلم. فإن كان قد أعلن ذلك وأظهره وقاله قولاً ذائعاً فيهم وجب أن ينقل ذلك نقل مثله مما شاع وذاع من نحو الصلوات وفرض الحج والصيام وغيرهما من العبادات التي لا اختلاف بين الأمة في أنها مشروعة مفروضة في دين النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ولا سيما إن كان فرض الإمامة من الفرائض العامة اللازمة لكل أحد في عينه وكان النص من النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أمراً عظيماً وخطراً جسيماً لا ينكتم مثله ولا يستتر عن الناس علمه مع العلم بأن الأمة قد نقلت بأسرها تولية النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم الإمرة لزيد بن حارثة ولأسامة بن زيد بن حارثة وعبد الله بن رواحة وعمرو بن العاص ولأبي موسى الأشعري وعمرو بن حزم وغير هؤلاء من أمرائه وقضاته حتى لم يذهب علمه على أحد من أهل العلم والأخبار. والنص منه على إمام على صفة ما تدعيه الشيعة من التصريح والإظهار أعظم وأخطر من تولية الأمراء والقضاة وتوفر الدواعي على نقله أكثر وإذا كان ذلك كذلك وجب لو كان الأمر على ما قالوه أن يغلب نقل النص من الكافة على كتمانه وأن يظهر وينقله خلف عن سلف إلى وقتنا هذا نقلاً شائعاً ذائعاً يكون أول نقلته ووسطهم وآخرهم سواء في أنهم جميعاً حجة يجب العلم عند [؟]
Chapter on the refutation of explicit designation (nass) and the establishment of election (ikhtiyar). If a questioner asks: 'What is the proof for your position of election for the community and the refutation of explicit designation for a specific Imam?' It is said to him: 'The proof for this is that if explicit designation is invalid from the two ways, and whichever one is invalid, election is valid, because the community agrees that there is no way to establish the Imamate except these two. And what indicates the invalidity of explicit designation is that if the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, had explicitly designated a specific Imam and obliged obedience to him upon the community to the exclusion of others, and said to them: 'This is my caliph and the Imam after me, so listen to him and obey,' it would not be free from either having said that and obligated it in the presence of the Companions or the majority of them, or in the presence of one or two or those whose report does not necessitate knowledge. If he had announced that and made it public and said it as a widespread statement among them, it would have been necessary that it be transmitted as a transmission like that which has spread and become widely known, such as the prayers, the obligation of Hajj, fasting, and other acts of worship concerning which there is no disagreement among the community that they are prescribed and obligatory in the religion of the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace. Especially since the obligation of the Imamate is among the universal obligations incumbent upon every individual, and the explicit designation from the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, would be a great matter and a serious affair, the like of which is not concealed nor is its knowledge hidden from people, while knowing that the community as a whole has transmitted the Prophet's appointment of Zayd ibn Haritha, Usamah ibn Zayd ibn Haritha, Abdullah ibn Rawahah, Amr ibn al-As, Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, Amr ibn Hazm, and others among his commanders and judges, such that its knowledge did not escape any of the people of knowledge and reports. And the explicit designation from him of an Imam of the description that the Shia claim regarding explicit statement and manifestation is greater and more serious than the appointment of commanders and judges, and the motives for its transmission are more numerous. And if that is the case, then if the matter were as they say, it would be necessary that the transmission of the explicit designation by the masses would overcome its concealment, and that it would become apparent and be transmitted by successors from predecessors until our time as a widespread, diffused transmission, whose first transmitters, middle ones, and last ones are equal in that all of them are a proof that necessitates knowledge of [?]
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Shia claim that the Prophet explicitly designated a specific Imam. Baqillani begins by stating the question: what is the proof for the Sunni position of election (ikhtiyar) and the refutation of explicit designation (nass)? He answers that the proof is that if nass is invalid, then ikhtiyar is valid, because the community agrees that there are only two ways to establish the Imamate: either by nass or by ikhtiyar. He then proceeds to prove the invalidity of nass. He argues that if the Prophet had designated a specific Imam and obligated obedience to him, he must have done so either in front of many companions or in front of only a few. If he had publicly announced it, then it would have been transmitted widely, just like other well-known obligations such as prayer, fasting, and hajj. The Imamate is an even more important matter, so its transmission would be even more widespread. The fact that the community has transmitted the Prophet's appointments of commanders like Zaid, Usamah, etc., but not any designation of an Imam, shows that no such designation occurred. The designation claimed by the Shia would be of even greater significance, yet it is not transmitted. Therefore, the only valid method is election.

Key Terms
النص
الاختيار
الإمامة
النقل
الشيعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the absence of transmission is not sufficient proof, because important matters can be forgotten or hidden.
Correction: Baqillani counters that the Imamate is of utmost importance, and if it had been designated, the motives for transmission would be even stronger than for appointments of commanders, which are well-known. Thus, absence of transmission is strong evidence.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what would have happened if the Prophet had explicitly designated an Imam in public?
A) It would have been transmitted widely like other obligations.
B) It would have been hidden by the companions.
C) It would only be known to a few.
D) It would have been written in the Quran.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani's argument hinges on the principle that important religious matters are transmitted widely; since the claimed designation is not, it must be false.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Baqillani argues that the Prophet’s commands on imamate would have been as widely transmitted as prayer and fasting. Are there any commands of the Prophet that you know about but neglect, treating them as less important than the pillars? Which one will you start acting on today?
?
The Shia claim that a small group preserved the true designation. Do you ever hold opinions that contradict the clear majority of scholars and the transmitted practice of the ummah? If so, what evidence do you have that is stronger than the widespread transmission of the sunnah?
?
If you truly believed that a single issue—like the imamate—was a matter of eternal salvation, would you base your certainty on claims that lack widespread transmission? Are there any beliefs you hold that rest on weak foundations? Will you examine them today with the same rigor Baqillani applies?

Refuting the Shi'a Claim of Explicit Nass for Ali's Imamate
Baqillani argues that the alleged nass on Ali fails due to lack of widespread transmission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's argument that the alleged explicit nass for Ali's imamate is false due to the lack of widespread transmission (tawatur) and the consensus of even Ali's supporters against it.

Core Idea
If the nass were real, it would be known necessarily—its absence proves its falsehood.

Baqillani takes on one of the central Shi'a claims: that the Prophet explicitly designated Ali as his successor. He argues that if such a nass existed, it would have been transmitted so widely that no one could deny it—yet even those who prefer Ali over others reject the nass. This lesson traces his argument and its reliance on the criterion of tawatur.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Shi'a claim
The Shi'a claim that the Prophet explicitly designated Ali as Imam through nass. Baqillani states that this nass would be more important than appointing governors, so motives to transmit it would be stronger.
2
Apply the criterion of tawatur
If the nass were true, it would have been transmitted widely (tawatur) and would produce necessary knowledge. Yet it did not—most Muslims deny it, and even many who favor Ali reject it.
This is the core of Baqillani's argument.
3
Consider the objection and response
An opponent might ask why such transmission would produce necessary knowledge. Baqillani refers to earlier proofs and notes that the Shi'a report lacks the characteristics of other well-known obligations.
4
Conclude the argument
Since the nass fails the test of tawatur and is denied even by Ali's admirers, it is invalid. This refutes the Shi'a claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والنص منه على إمام على صفة ما تدَّعيه الشيعة من التصريح والإظهار أعظم وأخطر من تولية الأمراء والقضاة وتوفر الدواعي على نقله أكثر وإذا كان ذلك كذلك وجب لو كان الأمر على ما قالوه أن يغلب نقل النص من الكافة على كتمانه وأن يظهر وينقله خلف عن سلف إلى وقتنا هذا نقلاً شائعاً ذائعاً يكون أول نقلته ووسطهم وآخِرُهم سواءٌ في أنهم جميعاً حجة يجب العلم عند نقلهم ولو كان ذلك كذلك لوجب أن يعلم ضرورة صدق الشيعة فيما تنقله النص وألا يوجد لهم مخالف الأمة يوفي [؟] على عددهم ينكر النص ويجحد من علمه كما لم يوجد فيها من ينكر فرض الصلاة والصيام وإمرة أسامة وزيد بن حارثة. وفي العلم ببطلان هذا ووجود أنفسنا غير مضطرة به ولا به وعلمنا بأن جمهور الأمة والسواد الأعظم منها ينكر ذلك ويجحده ويبرا من الدائن به ورأينا أكثر القائلين بفضل علي عليه السلام من الزيدية ومعتزلة البغاديين وغيرهم يُنْكِرُ النص عليه ويجحده مع تفضيله عليا على غيره وزوال التهمة عنه في بابه أوضح دليل على سقوط ما ذهبوا إليه وبطلانه. فإن قالوا: ولم قلتم إن ما هذه سبيله من النقل يُوجب علم الاضطرار؟ قيل لهم: قد بينا ذلك فيما قبل بما يُغني عن رده. وإذا لم يُنقل خبر الشيعة نقل مثله مما وقع شائعاً ذائعاً في الأصل ولا وجب العلم به كوجوب نظيره مما يَعُمُّ فرضُه والبلوى به ولا ارتفعت الشكوك والشبه فيه كارتفاعها عن نظيره وما جرى مجراه من تأمير النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لمن أمَّره وعقد القضاء لمن عقده بل ما يدعونه فوق هذا الباب ولا حصل علم ذلك لأكثر الشيعة والزيدية المُفضّلين لعلي عليه السلام على غيره من الأئمة والمختصين علماً بفضائله ومناقبه والمُبَرَّئين من التهمة في بابه عند الفريقين ولا وجب علمنا بما قالوه ضرورة ولا حصل أيضاً علمه لمن ليس من أهله مع بحثه عنه ممن يخالف الأمة كحصول علم اليهود والنصارى بمقدار فرض صلواتنا وصيامنا عند تلقيهم لنا وسماعهم لأخبارنا وجب القضاء على إبطال خبرهم عن النص بأكثر الأدلة
And the textual designation (nass) from him (the Prophet) regarding an Imam in the manner that the Shi'a claim of explicit declaration and manifestation is greater and more serious than the appointment of governors and judges, and the motives for its transmission are more abundant. If that is the case, then if the matter were as they say, it would be necessary that the transmission of the nass from the multitude would overcome its concealment, and that it would appear and be transmitted by successor from predecessor to our time as a widespread, disseminated transmission, such that its first transmitters, middle ones, and last ones are equal in that they are all a proof (hujja) by which knowledge must be had according to their transmission. If that were so, then it would be necessary that one know necessarily the truthfulness of the Shi'a in what they transmit of the nass, and that there would not exist for them any opponent from the community reaching [؟] their number who denies the nass and rejects it as is known, just as there does not exist among them one who denies the obligation of prayer and fasting and the command of Usama and Zayd ibn Haritha. And in knowing the falsehood of this, and our finding ourselves not compelled by it, and our knowledge that the majority of the community and the great mass of it deny that and reject it and disavow the one who adheres to it, and our seeing that most of those who affirm the virtue of Ali (peace be upon him) from the Zaydiyya and the Mu'tazila of Baghdad and others deny the nass upon him and reject it while preferring Ali over others and the removal of suspicion from him in this matter—this is the clearest evidence for the fall of what they have gone to and its falsehood. For if they say: Why do you say that such a transmission necessarily produces knowledge? It is said to them: We have already explained that before in what suffices to refute it. And if the report of the Shi'a has not been transmitted like others that occurred widespread and disseminated in origin, and knowledge of it has not become necessary like the necessity of knowledge of its counterpart which is universally obligatory and commonly tested, and the doubts and ambiguities concerning it have not been removed as they are removed from its counterpart and what runs its course from the Prophet's (peace be upon him) appointment of whom he appointed and his assignment of judgeship to whom he assigned—nay, what they claim is above this category—and knowledge of that has not occurred for most of the Shi'a and Zaydiyya who prefer Ali over other Imams and those specializing in knowledge of his virtues and merits and those free from suspicion in this matter according to both parties, and our knowledge of what they say has not become necessary, nor has knowledge of it occurred for those not of its people despite their investigation of it from those who oppose the community, like the knowledge of the Jews and Christians of the amount of our obligatory prayers and fasts when they receive from us and hear our reports, then judgment must be passed on the invalidity of their report concerning the nass by all evidences.
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Shi'a claim of explicit textual designation (nass) for Ali's imamate. Baqillani follows the order: (1) He argues that the alleged nass would be more momentous than appointing governors and judges, so it should have been transmitted even more widely. Since it was not, the claim fails. (2) If it were widely transmitted, it would produce necessary knowledge and there would be no dissenters; yet the majority of the community denies it. (3) Moreover, even those who prefer Ali—such as Zaydis and Baghdadi Mu'tazila—deny the nass, which is strong evidence against it. (4) An objection is raised: why does such transmission produce necessary knowledge? Baqillani answers that they have already explained this, and he elaborates: the Shi'a report lacks the characteristics of tawatur (widespread transmission) that other well-known obligations have, such as prayer and fasting and the appointments of Usama and Zayd. Even many Shi'a and Zaydis do not have necessary knowledge of it, and outsiders investigating do not acquire it either, just as Jews and Christians know about Muslim prayers through widespread report. Therefore, the claim is invalid.

النص (nass)
الشيعة (Shi'a)
الإمامة (imamate)
علم الضرورة (necessary knowledge)
التواتر (tawatur)
الزيدية (Zaydiyya)
المعتزلة (Mu'tazila)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the nass was hidden for political reasons
Correction: Baqillani argues that if it were real, it would be known necessarily by all, not hidden.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what does the fact that many who prefer Ali (like Zaydis and Mu'tazila) deny the nass indicate?
A) That they are not true Muslims
B) That the nass is true but they are ignorant
C) That the nass is false, since even those who favor Ali reject it
D) That they are biased against Ali

Key Takeaway
Baqillani refutes the Shi'a claim of explicit nass by showing that if it were true, it would be widely transmitted and produce necessary knowledge—but it is not, and even Ali's supporters reject it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You rely on widespread transmission for many of your beliefs in Islam—such as the obligation of prayer or the number of rak'ahs. Now ask yourself: is there any belief you hold that lacks such widespread testimony? How do you justify holding it? And what would Baqillani say to you?
?
Baqillani argued that if the nass were real, even the Jews and Christians would come to know it through our reports. Consider your own da'wah: do you live your convictions with such clarity and consistency that outsiders cannot help but recognize them? Or do you allow ambiguities that undermine the truth you claim?
?
The Zaydis and Mu'tazila—who preferred Ali—still rejected the nass because they saw no evidence for it. This shows that love for a person does not require accepting unsubstantiated claims about him. Is there a figure you revere so much that you are tempted to accept claims about them without evidence? How can you maintain love without compromising truth?

Proof of Falsehood of Shia Nass Claim
Baqillani refutes the Shia nass claim through a conditional argument and evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's argument that the Shia claim of explicit designation (nass) is false because if it were true it would be universally and necessarily known, and the actual state of the ummah shows the opposite.

Core Idea
Truth that is universally transmitted cannot be denied by the majority.

Baqillani presents a powerful logical argument against the Shia doctrine of explicit designation (nass) of Ali as the Prophet's successor. He uses the principle that if such a designation had occurred, it would have been transmitted widely and known necessarily to all, just like the obligations of prayer and fasting. Since in reality the great majority of the ummah, including many who preferred Ali, reject the nass, this proves the claim false. The passage also addresses a potential objection about the nature of necessity and transmission.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to understand the flow.
Notice the conditional structure starting with 'ولو كان ذلك كذلك'.
2
Identify the conditional argument
Baqillani begins with a hypothetical: if the nass were true, then necessary knowledge would follow and no one would deny it. Locate this conditional and its examples.
He compares with obligations like prayer and fasting which are universally known.
3
Observe the evidence against the condition
Baqillani points out that in reality the majority of the ummah denies the nass, and even those who prefer Ali (like the Zaydiyya and Mu'tazila) reject it. This shows the condition is not met.
The phrase 'السواد الأعظم' refers to the great majority.
4
Analyze the objection and response
The Shia might object that the nass is not the kind of transmission that necessitates necessary knowledge. Baqillani responds by comparing it to widely known matters and showing it lacks their characteristics.
He uses the analogy of Jews and Christians knowing Muslim prayers through widespread transmission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو كان ذلك كذلك لوجب أن يعلم ضرورة صدق الشيعة فيما تنقله من النص وألا يوجد لهم مخالف من الأمة يوفي على عددهم ينكر النص ويجحده ويجحد من علمه كما لم يوجد فيها من ينكر فرض الصلاة والصيام وإمرة أسامة وزيد بن حارثة. وفي العلم ببطلان هذا ووجود أنفسنا غير مضطرة به ولا به وعلمنا بأن جمهور الأمة والسواد الأعظم منها ينكر ذلك ويجحده ويبرا من الدائن به ورأينا أكثر القائلين بفضل علي عليه السلام من الزيدية ومعتزلة البغاديين وغيرهم يُنْكِرُ النص عليه ويجحده مع تفضيله عليا على غيره وزوال التهمة عنه في بابه أوضح دليل على سقوط ما ذهبوا إليه وبطلانه. فإن قالوا: ولم قلتم إن ما هذه سبيله من النقل يُوجب علم الاضطرار؟ قيل لهم: قد بينا ذلك فيما قَبلُ بما يُغْنى عن رده. وإذا لم يُنقل خبر الشيعة نقل مثله مما وقع شائعاً ذائعاً في الأصل ولا وجب العلم به كوجوب نظيره مما يَعُمُّ فرضُه والبلوى به ولا اترفعت الشكوك والشَّبَهُ فيه كارتفاعها عن نظيره وما جرى مجراه من تأمير النبي صلّى الله عليه وسلم لمنْ أمَّرَه وعقد القضاء لمن عقده بل ما يدعونه فوق هذا الباب ولا حَصَلَ علم ذلك لأكثر الشيعة والزيدية المُفضّلين لعلي عليه السلام على غيره من الأئمة والمختصين علماً بفضائله ومناقبه والمُبَرَّئين من التهمة في بابه عند الفريقين ولا وجب علمنا بما قالوه ضرورة ولا حصل أيضاً علمه لمن ليس من أهله مع بحثه عنه ممن يخالف الأمة كحصول علم اليهود والنصارى بمقدار فرض صلواتنا وصيامنا عند تلقيهم لنا وسماعهم لأخبارنا وجب القضاء على إبطال خبرهم عن النص بأكثر الأدلة الدالة على فساد الأخبار.
If that were the case, it would be necessary to know by necessity the truthfulness of the Shia in what they transmit of the nass, and that there would not exist among them any opponent from the ummah who exceeds them in number denying the nass and rejecting it and rejecting knowledge of it, just as there does not exist among them anyone who denies the obligation of prayer, fasting, and the appointment of Usama and Zayd ibn Haritha. And in knowing the falsehood of this, and finding ourselves not compelled by it nor by it, and our knowledge that the majority of the ummah and the great mass of it deny that and reject it and disavow those who adhere to it, and we see that most of those who say that Ali (peace be upon him) is superior among the Zaydiyya and the Baghdad Mu'tazila and others deny the nass upon him and reject it while preferring Ali over others, and the removal of suspicion from him in his chapter, is the clearest evidence of the collapse of what they claim and its falsehood. If they say: And why do you say that this kind of transmission necessitates necessary knowledge? It is said to them: We have already explained that previously with what suffices from repeating it. And since the report of the Shia is not transmitted as a similar report that occurred widely and spread in origin, nor is knowledge of it obligatory as its counterpart is obligatory that is general in obligation and common in occurrence, nor are doubts and ambiguities removed from it as they are removed from its counterpart and what is similar to it from the appointment by the Prophet (peace be upon him) of those he appointed and the designation of judiciary for those he designated; rather what they claim is above this category, and knowledge of that did not obtain for most of the Shia and the Zaydiyya who prefer Ali (peace be upon him) over others among the Imams and those specialized in knowledge of his virtues and merits and those free from suspicion in his chapter according to both groups, nor did our knowledge of what they say become necessary, nor did knowledge of it also obtain for those not of their people despite investigation by those who oppose the ummah, like the knowledge of the Jews and Christians of the amount of our prayers and fasting when they receive from us and hear our reports; then it is necessary to rule on invalidation of their report about the nass by the strongest evidence indicating the corruption of reports.
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage is a proof refuting the Shia claim of explicit designation (nass) of Ali as the Prophet's successor. Baqillani begins with a conditional: if the Shia claim were true, then the entire ummah would have necessarily known it and no one would deny it, just as no one denies the obligation of prayer or the appointments of Usama and Zayd. Since in reality the great majority of the ummah denies the nass and even many who prefer Ali (like the Zaydiyya and Baghdad Mu'tazila) reject the nass, this is clear evidence that the claim is false. He then addresses an anticipated objection: why does such transmission necessitate necessary knowledge? He dismisses it by saying the proof is already established. He elaborates: the Shia report is not transmitted like widely known matters; it does not produce certain knowledge even for most Shia themselves, nor for impartial researchers. By analogy, Jews and Christians know our prayers and fasting through widespread transmission; but the Shia nass is not like that. Therefore the Shia report is invalid.

Key Terms
النص
علم الضرورة
الخبر المتواتر
الإجماع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Shia claim that their transmission of nass is widespread and known necessarily by the community.
Correction: Baqillani demonstrates that the majority of the ummah denies it, and even many who prefer Ali reject the nass, showing it is not universally known.

Checkpoint
Why does Baqillani use the example of the obligations of prayer and fasting and the appointments of Usama and Zayd?
A) To show that these matters are known by necessity and universally accepted
B) To argue that Ali should have been appointed like them
C) To prove that the Shia claim is based on weak transmission
D) To refute the necessity of imamate

Key Takeaway
Baqillani refutes the Shia nass claim by showing that it fails the test of necessary and universal transmission, which is the hallmark of truly established religious knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are there any beliefs you hold that are not shared by the majority of Muslims? If so, how confident are you that they are true? Would you be willing to abandon them if clear evidence from the Quran and Sunnah proved otherwise?
?
The passage shows that even those who loved Ali rejected the nass because the evidence was not compelling. Think of a person or group you deeply admire. Is your loyalty to them stronger than your commitment to the truth? What would it cost you to follow the evidence against your attachments?
?
Baqillani argues that true knowledge compels agreement. Reflect on a time when you knew something was true from Islam but acted against it due to desire or peer pressure. What excuse did you use? How can you train yourself to submit to the truth immediately, even when it is difficult?

Why Khabar al-Wahid Cannot Confirm the Nass
Baqillani argues that even if the nass was reported by a few, it would still not produce certain knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a singular report (khabar al-wahid) cannot produce certain knowledge about the alleged designation of Ali, according to Imam Baqillani's argument.

Core Idea
Singular reports, even with many later narrators, cannot yield certainty about a momentous claim like the nass.

Baqillani continues his refutation by examining the nature of the transmission. He argues that even if the Prophet had designated Ali in front of a few people, that report cannot be taken as certain because the reporters are fallible and lack supporting guarantees. This lesson unpacks his reasoning and introduces a powerful argument from the strength of motives to transmit.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to understand the argument flow.
Notice the two-part structure: first refuting certainty, then the argument from motives.
2
Identify Baqillani's reasons
List all the reasons Baqillani gives for why a single report about the nass does not produce certain knowledge. He mentions several: fallibility of reporters, lack of divine/prophetic confirmation, no consensus, reason not demanding it, etc.
These reasons are the core of the first part of the passage.
3
Examine the motives argument
Look at the second part where Baqillani argues that if the nass had occurred, the strong motives to transmit it would have led to widespread knowledge. Compare this to the transmission of the Ansar's dispute.
This is a key epistemological argument based on social transmission dynamics.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Even though the passage ends mid-sentence, reflect on how the motives argument implies that the lack of widespread transmission proves the claim false.
Baqillani uses this to undermine the Shia claim of a hidden nass.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كان الرسول صلّى الله عليه وسلم إنما نص عليه النص الذي يدعونه بمحضر من الواحد والاثنين ومن يجوز الكذب والسهو عليه ولم يُذع ذلك ويُشِعهُ فلا سبيل إذاً لنا إلى العلم والقطع على أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم نص على رجـل بعينـه وأَلْزَمَ فَرْضَ طاعته دون غيره إذ كان إنما نقل ذلك في الأصل عن الرسول صلّى الله عليه وسلم من لا يجب العلم بصدقه ومَنْ يجوز دخول الغَلَطِ والسِّهْوِ عليه وكنا نحن وأنتم قد اتفقنا على أن أخبار الآحاد لا توجب علم الاضطرار وإن كان الأخذون عنهم ممن عددهم كعدد القطر والرمل فلم يقارن أيضاً خبر ذلك الواحد عن النبي صلّى الله عليه وسلم ما يدل على صدقه بأن يخبر الله تعالى عن ذلك الواحد في نص كتابه أنه لا يكذِبُ في شيء من أخباره أو يُخبر بذلك الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم مِن أمْرِه أو تُجمِعَ الأمَّةُ على تلقي خبره بالقبول والمصير إلى العلم بموجبه والقطع عليه ولا كانت العقول دالة على وجوب النص من الله ورسوله على ذلك الرجل بعينه ومُقْتَضيةً لصِدْقِ المخبرين عن النص عليه ولا ادّعى ذلك الواحد والأحاد على سائر الأمة أو على من لا يجوز عليه فيها الكذب والافتعال والإمساك عن إنكار كذب يُدعى عليهم أنهم حضروا نصَّ النبي صلّى الله عليه وسلم على مَنْ ادعي النص عليه وسمعوه كما سمعه فإذا قد عَرِي خبر الواحد عن النص عن كل شيء يدل على صدق أخبار الآحاد فوجب ألا نقطع بذلك ولا نصير إلى علمه بخبر الواحد. وعلى أنه لو كان النص قد رواه واحد وآحاد عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في صدر الأمة وادعى مع روايتهم حضورهم له وسماعهم فالواجب أن يقع لنا العلم ضَرُورة بأن هذا الأمر الخطير والشأن العظيم قد ادعاه ورواه راو في صدر الإسلام وأنه قد استشهد عليه وأيده بدعواه حُضُور القوم له وسماعهم إياه لأن توفر الدواعي على نقل ذلك، لو كان صحيحاً، أشدُّ من توفرها على نقل خلاف الأنصار في الإمامة وقول قائلها: «أنا جُذَيْلها المُحَكِّكُ وعُذَيْقُها
And if the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) only made the nass that they claim in the presence of one or two persons, and those upon whom lying and forgetfulness are possible, and he did not make that public and spread it, then there is no way for us to know and be certain that the Prophet (peace be upon him) designated a specific man and obligated obedience to him exclusively, since originally that was only transmitted from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) by one whose truthfulness is not necessarily known, and upon whom error and forgetfulness may enter. And we and you have agreed that singular reports do not necessitate necessary knowledge, even if those who receive from them are as numerous as drops of rain or grains of sand. Moreover, the report of that single person from the Prophet (peace be upon him) is not accompanied by anything indicating his truthfulness, such as God Almighty informing in the text of His Book that that person never lies in any of his reports, or the Messenger (peace be upon him) informing about his affair, or the consensus of the ummah to accept his report and proceed to knowledge of its content and certainty about it. Nor do the intellects indicate the necessity of nass from God and His Messenger upon that specific man, nor necessitate the truthfulness of those who report the nass upon him. Nor did that single person or the few individuals claim against the rest of the ummah, or against those upon whom lying and fabrication and refraining from denying falsehood are not possible, that they witnessed the Prophet's (peace be upon him) nass upon the one claimed to have the nass and heard it as he heard it. Thus the report of the single person about the nass is devoid of everything that indicates the truthfulness of singular reports, so it is necessary that we not be certain about that nor arrive at knowledge of it through the report of a single person. And if the nass had been narrated by one or a few from the Prophet (peace be upon him) in the early community, and they claimed along with their narration their presence and hearing it, then it would be necessary for knowledge to occur to us necessarily that this grave matter and great affair had been claimed and narrated by a narrator in early Islam, and that he had called witnesses and supported his claim by the presence of the people and their hearing it, because the motives to transmit that, if it were true, would be stronger than the motives to transmit the dispute of the Ansar about the imamate and the saying of its speaker: 'I am its stub that scratches and its date-palm...'
Source pages p. 449

Commentary
This passage is a continuation of Baqillani's refutation, now focusing on the nature of the transmission as khabar al-wahid (single report). He argues that even if the Prophet had designated Ali in front of one or two people, that report would not produce certain knowledge because such reporters are fallible. He reminds that both parties agree that ahad reports do not yield necessary knowledge, no matter how many later transmitters there are (if the original source is one). Moreover, there is no divine guarantee of the reporter's reliability, no prophetic confirmation, and no consensus to accept such a report. Reason itself does not demand that the nass occurred. Additionally, the reporters could not claim that the whole ummah witnessed it. Therefore, no certainty can be reached. He then adds a new argument: if the nass had been narrated by a few in the early community, and they claimed to have witnessed it, then necessary knowledge would arise that such a claim was made, because the motives to transmit such a momentous event would be extremely strong—even stronger than the transmission of the Ansar's dispute about the caliphate. This implies that if the nass were true, its transmission would have been widespread, and the fact that it is not is evidence of its falsehood. The passage ends with an incomplete quote from the Ansar's saying.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد
علم الاضطرار
القرائن
توفر الدواعي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A report from one or two reliable companions can establish certainty about the nass.
Correction: Baqillani argues that such a report lacks the indicators needed for certainty, and its truth cannot be assumed because the reporters are fallible and no external guarantee exists.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, why does the report of a single person about the nass not produce certain knowledge?
A) Because the Prophet only spoke in private
B) Because the reporter is fallible and there is no divine guarantee of his truthfulness
C) Because the Shia are not reliable
D) Because the nass was never intended to be public

Key Takeaway
Khabar al-wahid, without accompanying indicators of truthfulness, cannot produce certain knowledge about momentous claims like the nass, and the lack of widespread transmission itself indicates the claim's falsehood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You rely on many religious claims that you have not personally witnessed. How does Baqillani's standard for certainty challenge you to examine the strength of the evidence behind your own foundational beliefs? Will you seek stronger proofs, or are you content with probability?
?
Imagine you are presented with a report that a major event occurred that changes your entire worldview, but it comes from only one or two sources. Would you accept it? What would it take for you to be certain? This lesson demands you consider: do you treat the nass claim fairly, or do you apply a different standard to your own cherished beliefs?
?
Baqillani argues that if the nass were true, it would have been widely transmitted despite any obstacles. Think of a truth you know is important but hesitate to share or act upon. Are you fulfilling the obligation to transmit what you know? Or are you like those who remained silent, and does that silence itself testify against the truth of your claim?

Why Isolated Reports Cannot Prove the Shi'a Claim of Explicit Designation
Baqillani argues that the Shi'a claim of explicit designation (nass) cannot be established by khabar al-wahid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's argument that the Shi'a claim of explicit designation (nass) cannot be established through isolated reports (khabar al-wahid) because such reports do not produce certain knowledge.

Core Idea
No isolated report can prove a matter of foundational importance like the Imamate.

In this passage, Imam Baqillani refutes the Shi'a claim that the Prophet explicitly designated Ali as his successor. He does not simply reject the claim; he demonstrates why the very nature of the evidence—isolated reports—cannot support such a crucial doctrine. Let's examine his argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once fully. Notice Baqillani's style: he starts by stating the corruption of the reports.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the key principle
Find where Baqillani reminds the reader that isolated reports (khabar al-wahid) do not produce necessary knowledge (ilm al-iddiraar). This is the core epistemological principle.
This principle is agreed upon by both sides.
3
Follow the conditional argument
Baqillani uses a hypothetical: even if the Prophet made the designation, it was not publicized, and the transmitter could be unreliable. Thus, we cannot be certain.
He also lists missing indicators of truthfulness.
4
Consider the hypothetical scenario
Baqillani argues that if the claim were true, motives for transmission would have been overwhelming, leading to tawatur. Since it didn't happen, the claim is false.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدالة على فساد الأخبار. وهذا بين لمن نصح نفسه وإن كان الرسول صلّى الله عليه وسلم إنما نص عليه النص الذي يدعونه بمحضر من الواحد والاثنين ومن يجوز الكذب والسهو عليه ولم يُذع ذلك ويُشِعهُ فلا سبيل إذاً لنا إلى العلم والقطع على أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم نص على رجل بعينه وأَلْزَمَ فَرْضَ طاعته دون غيره إذ كان إنما نقل ذلك في الأصل عن الرسول صلّى الله عليه وسلم من لا يجب العلم بصدقه ومَنْ يجوز دخول الغَلَطِ والسِّهْوِ عليه وكنا نحن وأنتم قد اتفقنا على أن أخبار الآحاد لا توجب علم الاضطرار وإن كان الأخذون عنهم ممن عددهم كعدد القطر والرمل فلم يقارن أيضاً خبر ذلك الواحد عن النبي صلّى الله عليه وسلم ما يدل على صدقه بأن يخبر الله تعالى عن ذلك الواحد في نص كتابه أنه لا يكذِبُ في شيء من أخباره أو يُخبر بذلك الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم مِن أمْرِه أو تُجمِعَ الأمَّةُ على تلقي خبره بالقبول والمصير إلى العلم بموجبه والقطع عليه ولا كانت العقول دالة على وجوب النص من الله ورسوله على ذلك الرجل بعينه ومُقْتَضيةً لصِدْقِ المخبرين عن النص عليه ولا ادّعى ذلك الواحد والأحاد على سائر الأمة أو على من لا يجوز عليه فيها الكذب والافتعال والإمساك عن إنكار كذب يُدعى عليهم أنهم حضروا نصَّ النبي صلّى الله عليه وسلم على مَنْ ادعي النص عليه وسمعوه كما سمعه فإذا قد عَرِي خبر الواحد عن النص عن كل شيء يدل على صدق أخبار الآحاد فوجب ألا نقطع بذلك ولا نصير إلى علمه بخبر الواحد . وعلى أنه لو كان النص قد رواه واحد وآحاد عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في صدر الأمة وادعى مع روايتهم حضورهم له وسماعهم فالواجب أن يقع لنا العلم ضرورة بأن هذا الأمر الخطير والشأن العظيم قد ادعاه ورواه راو في صدر الإسلام وأنه قد استشهد عليه وأيده بدعواه حضور القوم له وسماعهم إياه لأن توفر الدواعي على نقل ذلك، لو كان صحيحاً، أشدّ من توفرها على نقل خلاف الأنصار في الإمامة وقول قائلها: «أنا جُذَيْلها المُحَكِّكُ وعُذَيْقُها المُرجي» ونقل رواية من روى قول النبي صلّى الله عليه وسلم: «الأئمةُ من قريش»، وأن محمداً صلى الله عليه وسلم رأى ربه بعيني رأسه.
That which indicates the corruption of reports. And this is clear for whoever advises himself. Even if the Messenger, peace be upon him, supposedly made the textual designation (nass) which they claim in the presence of one or two persons, or someone upon whom lying and forgetfulness are possible, and he did not make it public and spread it, then there is no way for us to have certain knowledge and be definitive that the Prophet, peace be upon him, designated a specific man and made it obligatory to obey him excluding others, since that was originally transmitted from the Messenger, peace be upon him, only by one whose truthfulness is not necessarily known, and upon whom error and forgetfulness are possible. And we and you have agreed that isolated reports (akhbar al-ahad) do not necessitate necessary knowledge (ilm al-idtirar), even if those who received them are as numerous as raindrops and sand. So the report of that single person from the Prophet, peace be upon him, was not accompanied by anything indicating his truthfulness—such as God Almighty informing about that single person in the text of His Book that he does not lie in any of his reports, or the Messenger informing about him, or the ummah agreeing to receive his report with acceptance and to act upon it with certainty and finality. Nor did intellects indicate the necessity of a designation from God and His Messenger upon that specific man, and necessitate the truthfulness of those reporting that designation. Nor did that single person or a few claim against the rest of the ummah—or against those upon whom lying, fabrication, and silence about denying lies attributed to them are not permissible—that they were present at the Prophet's designation upon the one alleged to be designated and heard it as he heard it. So when the report of the single person concerning the designation has been stripped of everything indicating the truthfulness of isolated reports, it is necessary that we not be definitive about that nor arrive at knowledge of it through an isolated report. Moreover, if the designation had been narrated by one or a few from the Prophet in the early period of the ummah, and they claimed along with their narration that they were present and heard it, then it would be necessary for us to have necessary knowledge that this serious matter and great affair was claimed and narrated by a narrator in early Islam, and that he testified and supported it by his claim of the people's presence and hearing of it, because the motives for transmitting that—if it were true—would be stronger than the motives for transmitting the dispute of the Ansar about leadership and the saying of its speaker: 'I am its firmly-knit club and its branch that is deferred.' And the transmission of the narration of one who narrated the Prophet's saying: 'The leaders are from Quraysh,' and that Muhammad saw his Lord with the eyes of his head.
Source pages p. 449

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Shi'a claim that the Prophet explicitly designated Ali as his successor (nass). Baqillani argues from the nature of transmission. He begins by stating that the argument clearly shows the corruption of the Shi'a reports. He then points out that even if the Prophet made such a designation, it was supposedly done in front of only one or two people, or someone unreliable. Crucially, it was not publicized. Therefore, we cannot have certain knowledge of it. The report comes from a transmitter whose truthfulness is not guaranteed and who could err. Baqillani then reminds the reader of the agreed-upon principle that isolated reports (khabar al-wahid) do not produce necessary knowledge (ilm al-darura), even if many people later accept them. For the report to be credible, it would need divine confirmation (e.g., God stating the narrator is truthful in the Qur'an), prophetic endorsement, or unanimous acceptance by the ummah—none of which exists. Additionally, reason does not demand such a designation. The single narrator or a few did not challenge the rest of the ummah to produce witnesses. Thus, the report lacks any indicator of truthfulness. He then presents a hypothetical: if such an important claim were true, it would have been transmitted widely (tawatur) because the motives for transmission would be overwhelming—even more so than the well-known dispute at Saqifa or the famous reports about the Quraysh or the vision of Allah. Since it was not widely transmitted, it cannot be true.

Key Terms
أخبار الآحاد
النص
علم الاضطرار
التواتر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Baqillani argue that the claim of nass (explicit designation) fails to produce certain knowledge?
A) Because the narrators were all weak and unknown.
B) Because it is based on isolated reports without corroboration that would necessitate necessary knowledge.
C) Because the Qur'an explicitly denies such a designation.
D) Because the companions unanimously rejected it.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani shows that the claim of explicit designation fails because it relies on isolated reports that lack the indicators of truthfulness required for certain knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you accept a religious claim from a scholar or teacher, do you verify it against the same standard Baqillani applies here—requiring widespread transmission and clear indicators of truth? Or do you rely on blind trust? What would it mean to 'advise yourself' in your own search for truth?
?
Consider a belief you hold that is not widely accepted by mainstream orthodoxy. If you applied Baqillani's criterion of tawatur, would that belief stand? If not, are you willing to reconsider it?
?
The Prophet's mission was public; he had no 'hidden teachings.' Does your own faith community have any claims based on obscure or isolated reports? How exposed are you to the danger of following nass claims without 'every indicator of truth'? What step will you take today to ensure your beliefs are grounded in certainty?
