Refuting Taqiyya and Proving Abu Bakr's Caliphate
Argues that Ali's praise contradicts taqiyya and cites hadiths proving Abu Bakr's caliphate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Baqillani uses Ali's own statements and prophetic hadiths to refute the Shia claim of taqiyya and to establish Abu Bakr's rightful caliphate.

Core Idea
Consistent praise cannot be dissimulation; hadiths point to Abu Bakr's leadership.

In this passage, Imam al-Baqillani builds a two-part argument. First, he demonstrates that Ali's well-known praise of Abu Bakr, Umar, and Uthman cannot be explained away as taqiyya (dissimulation) because it would be logically inconsistent with the claim that Ali was wronged. Then, he presents four hadiths from the Prophet that explicitly indicate Abu Bakr's leadership, providing clear textual evidence for his caliphate.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the full translation. Absorb the author's argumentative flow.
Notice the two distinct sections: refutation of taqiyya and hadith evidence.
2
Identify the logical argument against taqiyya
Find the key conditional: if the Prophet had designated Ali, then Ali would not have praised the caliphs. This is the core refutation.
The claim of taqiyya would also entail slander against the Imams.
3
Examine the hadiths cited
List the four hadiths: leading prayer, 'Allah refuses except Abu Bakr', 'companions of Yusuf', and 'follow Abu Bakr and Umar'. Note how each supports Abu Bakr's authority.
These are presented as direct proofs (nass) for Abu Bakr's caliphate.
4
Reflect on the overall structure
Consider how the first part clears away the taqiyya objection, paving the way for the hadith evidence to stand uncontested.
This is a standard method: remove counterarguments before presenting positive proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في نظائر هذه الأقاويل المشهورة عنه في مدحهم وتقريظهم وحس الثناء عليهم وأنه راض بإمامتهم وأنه لو كان الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم قد نص عليه وقطع العذر في بابه لم يجز أنه يقول فيمن غصبه وجحده حقه هذه الأقاويل وتكون أفعاله معهم واقتداؤه بهم ما ذكرنا فكيف تركتم هذا الظاهر المعلوم من قوله وفعله إلى تعليل النفوس وشهواتها وتسويفها للأماني ؟ فإن قالوا : كل هذا الذي ظهر منه على سبيل التقية والإرهاب والخوف منهم قيل لهم : وما الحجة في ذلك مع ما فيه من القدح وسوء القول في أمي والمؤمنين؟ فلا يجدون في ذلك متعلقاً. ثم يقال لهم : كيف لم تستدلوا على إثبات النص لأبي بكر رضي الله عنه بقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : «يوم الناس أبو بكر»، وقوله : «يأبى الله ورسوله والمسلمون إلا أبا بكر»، وقوله لعائشة : «إنكن صواحبات يوسف يأبى الله إلا أبا بكر»، وقوله : «اقتدوا باللذين من بعدي أبي بكر وعمر».
In the like of these well-known statements from him (Ali) praising them, commending them, and extolling them, and that he was pleased with their leadership, and that if the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) had explicitly designated him (Ali) and cut off the excuse regarding him, it would not be permissible for him to say these statements about those who (allegedly) usurped his right and denied him his right, and his actions with them and his following them were as we mentioned. So how can you abandon this manifest and known evidence from his words and deeds and turn to the whims of souls and their desires and the postponement of hopes? If they say: All of this that appeared from him was out of dissimulation (taqiyya) and intimidation and fear of them, it is said to them: What is the proof for that, given the condemnation and ill-speaking about the Imams and the believers that it entails? They will find no basis for that. Then it is said to them: Why have you not used as evidence for the establishment of the textual designation (nass) for Abu Bakr, may Allah be pleased with him, his statement (peace be upon him): 'The one who leads the people in prayer is Abu Bakr,' and his statement: 'Allah and His Messenger and the Muslims refuse except Abu Bakr,' and his statement to Aisha: 'You are the companions of Yusuf; Allah refuses except Abu Bakr,' and his statement: 'Follow the two after me: Abu Bakr and Umar.'
Source pages p. 469

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Shia argument that Ali's apparent acceptance of the caliphs was due to taqiyya (dissimulation). The author begins by summarizing the previous evidence: numerous well-known statements from Ali praising Abu Bakr, Umar, and Uthman, commending them, and expressing pleasure with their leadership. The author then presents a logical argument: if the Prophet had explicitly designated Ali as his successor (nass) and left no excuse for others, it would be impossible for Ali to utter such praise about those who supposedly usurped his right, and his actions would be inconsistent with his alleged oppression. Therefore, the manifest evidence from Ali's words and deeds must be accepted. The author rebukes those who abandon this clear evidence in favor of subjective desires and wishful thinking. He then anticipates an objection: the Shia might claim that Ali's behavior was out of taqiyya, fear, and intimidation. The author counters that this claim itself is baseless and amounts to slander against the Imams and believers. He then shifts to direct evidence for Abu Bakr's caliphate, citing four hadiths: the Prophet's statement that Abu Bakr should lead the prayer, the report that the Prophet said 'Allah and His Messenger and the Muslims refuse except Abu Bakr' (regarding the caliphate), the hadith to Aisha about being 'the companions of Yusuf' but that Allah refuses except Abu Bakr, and the command to follow Abu Bakr and Umar after him. These hadiths serve as explicit textual proofs for Abu Bakr's right to the caliphate.

Key Terms
التقية
النص
الإمامة
الخلافة
القدح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ali's praise of the caliphs was only out of taqiyya and fear, so it does not reflect his true opinion.
Correction: The author argues that if Ali had been wronged, he would not have consistently praised those who wronged him; the taqiyya claim leads to slander of the Imams and has no basis.

Checkpoint
What is the main logical argument the author uses to refute the claim that Ali acted out of taqiyya?
A) Hadiths prove Ali was always truthful
B) If Ali was wronged, he would not have praised his oppressors
C) Taqiyya is forbidden in Islam
D) The Prophet explicitly forbade dissimulation

Key Takeaway
Ali's consistent praise refutes the taqiyya claim, and prophetic hadiths establish Abu Bakr's caliphate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When your actions and words consistently show something, do you still allow yourself to hide behind excuses of fear or circumstance, even when the evidence is clear? What would it cost you to align your inner beliefs with your outer reality?
?
In what area of your faith are you clinging to wishful thinking or emotional attachments rather than accepting what is manifest from the Quran and Sunnah? Will you today surrender that desire to the truth?
?
If you were in Ali's position and knew the truth, would you have had the courage to act consistently with it despite pressure from others? What does your answer reveal about the strength of your own conviction?

The Prophet's Praise Refutes Secret Designation
The author argues that the Prophet's praise of Abu Bakr and Umar is incompatible with a secret designation for Ali, and refutes the taqiyya objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Prophet's consistent praise of Abu Bakr and Umar refutes the claim of a secret designation for Ali, and why the taqiyya objection fails.

Core Idea
The Prophet's public praise contradicts a secret succession plan.

This passage presents a key Sunni argument against the Shi'a claim that the Prophet explicitly designated Ali as his successor. The author, Imam al-Baqillani, cites multiple authentic hadith where the Prophet praises Abu Bakr and Umar in the highest terms. He then argues that such praise would be impossible if these Companions had usurped Ali's right. The passage also anticipates and refutes the objection that the Prophet acted out of taqiyya (dissimulation) and fear.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and cited hadiths
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Pay close attention to the hadiths quoted about Abu Bakr and Umar.
The hadiths include: 'The best of this nation after its Prophet is Abu Bakr, then Umar...' and 'These two are the masters of the elderly of Paradise.'
2
Understand the logical argument
The author argues that if the Prophet had secretly designated Ali, he would not have praised those who allegedly usurped Ali's right. This contradiction shows the designation claim is false.
Consider the principle: a consistent person does not praise usurpers while remaining silent about the usurped.
3
Examine the taqiyya objection and refutation
The opponents may claim the Prophet's praise was out of fear. The author counters that this would imply the Prophet lied or slandered, which is impossible for a prophet.
The refutation hinges on the Prophet's integrity and the honor of the Believers.

('Inadvertence is more beloved to me than this covered one.' And his statement in the narration of Suwayd ibn al-Jamm al-Ghafir from his companions: 'Indeed, the best of this nation after its Prophet is Abu Bakr, then after Abu Bakr is Umar, then Allah knows best where the good is.' And his narration from the Prophet ﷺ that he said to them: 'These two are the masters of the elderly of the people of Paradise among the first and the last, except for the prophets and messengers.' And his statement: 'No one informed me about the Messenger of Allah ﷺ except that I made him swear an oath, except Abu Bakr; and Abu Bakr told me, and Abu Bakr was truthful.' There are similar well-known statements of his praising them, extolling them, and commending them, and that he was satisfied with their leadership, and that if the Messenger of Allah ﷺ had designated him (Ali) and cut off excuse regarding his case, it would not be permissible for him to say these things about one who usurped him and denied his right, and for his actions with them and his following them to be as we mentioned. If they say: 'All this that appeared from him was out of dissimulation (taqiyya), intimidation, and fear of them,' then it is said to them: 'What proof is there for that, given that it involves disparagement and evil speech about the Mother of the Believers and the believers?' Source pages p. 469

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Shi'a claim that the Prophet explicitly designated Ali as his successor. The author begins by citing several well-known hadith in which the Prophet praises Abu Bakr and Umar, stating that Abu Bakr is the best of the community after the Prophet, then Umar, and that they are the masters of the elderly of Paradise, etc. The author then argues that if the Prophet had indeed made a clear designation (nass) and removed all excuse regarding the succession of Ali, it would not be possible for him to utter such praise about those who allegedly usurped Ali's right and denied him his due, nor would his actions and following them be as described. Therefore, the author asks rhetorically: why have you abandoned this manifest evidence from his words and deeds in favor of interpreting according to whims and desires? Then the author anticipates the objection that the Prophet's outward actions were done out of taqiyya (dissimulation) and fear. The author counters this by stating: what proof do you have for that claim, especially considering that it impugns the Prophet and the believers? Thus, the opponents have no basis for such an objection. The passage ends with the conclusion that this excuse is untenable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet's praise of Abu Bakr and Umar could have been out of taqiyya (dissimulation) and fear.
Correction: Taqiyya would require the Prophet to falsely praise usurpers, which impugns his truthfulness and disparages the Believers, so it is not a valid excuse.

Checkpoint

A) It proves that the Prophet secretly designated Ali.
B) It contradicts the claim of a secret designation because the Prophet would not have praised those who allegedly usurped Ali's right.
C) It shows that the Prophet was forced to praise them out of fear.
D) It indicates that Abu Bakr and Umar were more virtuous than Ali.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's public praise of Abu Bakr and Umar is strong evidence against the claim of a secret designation for Ali.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever held a belief about a religious figure or historical event based on what you wanted to be true, rather than what the clear evidence shows? How does this lesson's call to follow the 'apparent known evidence' (الظاهر المعلوم) challenge you to examine your own sources of conviction?
?
If you were in a position where your public words contradicted a private commitment, would you have the courage to be consistent like the Prophet (as argued here)? What might be holding you back from aligning your outward speech with your inner convictions?
?
The author argues that claiming the Prophet acted out of taqiyya would impugn his honor. When you explain away difficult evidence by accusing others of insincerity, do you realize how that reflects on your own character? What change must you make today to stop rationalizing what you already know to be true?

Prophetic Statements as Proof for Abu Bakr's Caliphate
The author argues that the Prophet's words constitute textual evidence (nass) for Abu Bakr's caliphate, and asks why the opposition does not accept this.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Baqillani uses a series of prophetic hadith to argue that the caliphate of Abu Bakr is established by explicit textual designation (nass).

Core Idea
Multiple prophetic statements constitute explicit textual evidence for leadership.

Imam Baqillani presents a powerful argument: the Prophet ﷺ left numerous explicit statements that point to Abu Bakr as his successor. In this passage, he lists these statements and challenges the opposition: if these are not clear evidence, then what is? We will examine this argument and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse each hadith. Notice the structure: a rhetorical question followed by a list of statements.
The passage is dense with hadith; focus on the author's cumulative argument.
2
Identify the types of hadith
The author lists several categories: direct commands ('the imam is Abu Bakr'), statements of preference ('Allah refuses except Abu Bakr'), and prophecies ('the caliphate is thirty years'). Group them mentally.
3
Understand the rhetorical challenge
The author ends with 'So why did you not affirm the nass for them both?' This is a refutation of those who deny explicit designation. Ask yourself: what answer could the opposition give?
This step connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقال لهم : كيف لم تستدلوا على إثبات النص لأبي بكر رضي الله عنه بقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : «يوم الناس أبو بكر (ه)، وقوله : «يأبى الله ورسوله والمسلمون إلا أبا بكر » (٦) ، وقوله لعائشة : «إنكن صواحبات يوسف يأبى الله إلا أبا بكر (٧) ، وقوله : «اقتدوا باللذين من بعدي أبي بكر وعمر» (۸) ، وقوله : «لا ينبغي لقوم يكون فيهم أبو بكر أن يتقدمهم غيره (۱)، وقوله : «إيتوني بدواة وكتف أكتب لأبي بكر كتاباً لا يختلف عليه اثنان» (۲)، وقوله صلى الله عليه: «أنتما من الدين بمنزلة السمع والبصر من الرأس» (۳) ، وقوله : لو كنت متخذاً خليلاً لاتخذت أبا بكر خليلاً ولكن صاحبكم خليل الرحمن» (4) ، وقوله : «إن تولوها أبا بكر تجدوه ضعيفاً في بدنه قوياً في أمر الله وإن تولوها عمر تجدوه قوياً في بدنه قوياً في أمر الله وإن تولوها علياً تجدوه هادياً مهدياً وعلموا بهذه البنية والترتيب أنه قصد التنبي، على النص عليه، وبقوله : «الخلافة بعدي إلى ثلاثين» (۹) ، وقوله : «إن يطع الناس أبا بكر وعمر رشدوا . ورشدت أمتهم ؛ وإن يعصوهما غووا وغوت أمتهم» (١) ، وقوله : «خير أمتي أبو بكر ثم عمر ، وقوله : «من أفضل من أبي بكر؟ زوجني ابنته وجهزني بماله وجاهد معي ساعة الخوف ؛ وقوله في عمر: «لو كان بعدي نبي لكان عمر (۷) ، و لو لم أُبعث فيكم لبعثَ عمر (۷) ، و «إن الله ضرب «لولم » بالحق على لسان عمر وقلبه يقول الحق وإن كان مرا (۸) ، و إن منكم لمحدثين ومكلمين وإن عمر منهم) (۱) منهم» (١) ، في نظائر هذه الأخبار والفضائل التي يطول تتبعها؛ فكيف لم تقولوا بالنص عليهما؟ .
Then it is said to them: How did you not infer the proof of the textual designation (nass) for Abu Bakr, may Allah be pleased with him, from his statement ﷺ: 'The imam of the people is Abu Bakr,' and his statement: 'Allah, His Messenger, and the Muslims refuse except Abu Bakr,' and his statement to Aisha: 'You are the companions of Yusuf; Allah refuses except Abu Bakr,' and his statement: 'Follow the two after me: Abu Bakr and Umar,' and his statement: 'It is not fitting for a people among whom is Abu Bakr that anyone else should precede them,' and his statement: 'Bring me an inkwell and a shoulder blade so that I may write a document for Abu Bakr after which two will not differ,' and his statement ﷺ: 'You two are to the religion as hearing and sight are to the head,' and his statement: 'If I were to take a close friend, I would take Abu Bakr as a close friend, but your companion is the friend of the Merciful,' and his statement: 'If you entrust it to Abu Bakr, you will find him weak in his body but strong in the command of Allah; if you entrust it to Umar, you will find him strong in his body and strong in the command of Allah; if you entrust it to Ali, you will find him a guided guide,' and they understood from this structure and arrangement that he intended to indicate the designation (nass) upon him (Abu Bakr), and by his statement: 'The caliphate after me is for thirty [years],' and his statement: 'If the people obey Abu Bakr and Umar, they will be guided and their nation will be guided; if they disobey them, they will go astray and their nation will go astray,' and his statement: 'The best of my nation is Abu Bakr, then Umar,' and his statement: 'Who is more virtuous than Abu Bakr? He married me to his daughter, equipped me with his wealth, and strove with me in the hour of fear,' and his statement about Umar: 'If there were to be a prophet after me, it would be Umar,' and 'Had I not been sent among you, Umar would have been sent,' and 'Indeed, Allah has placed the truth on the tongue of Umar and his heart; he speaks the truth even if it is bitter,' and 'Indeed, among you are those who are inspired and spoken to, and Umar is among them,' and similar reports and virtues whose enumeration would be lengthy. So why did you not affirm the textual designation (nass) for them both?
Source pages p. 469

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of explicit prophetic statements that the author argues constitute textual evidence (nass) for the caliphate of Abu Bakr (and by extension Umar). The author begins by saying: 'Then it is said to them: why did you not infer the proof of the designation (nass) for Abu Bakr from the following statements of the Prophet?' He then lists a series of hadith: 'The imam of the people is Abu Bakr,' 'Allah, His Messenger, and the Muslims refuse except Abu Bakr,' 'You are like the companions of Yusuf; Allah refuses except Abu Bakr,' 'Follow the two after me: Abu Bakr and Umar,' 'It is not fitting for a people among whom is Abu Bakr that anyone else should lead them,' 'Bring me a writing instrument so that I may write a document for Abu Bakr after which two will not differ,' 'You two are to the religion as hearing and sight are to the head,' 'If I were to take a close friend, I would take Abu Bakr, but your companion is the friend of the Merciful,' 'If you entrust it to Abu Bakr... if you entrust it to Umar... if you entrust it to Ali...' and he notes that this demonstrates intention of designation. He includes statements about the caliphate being thirty years, obedience to Abu Bakr and Umar leading to guidance, their superiority, and specific virtues of Umar such as 'If there were a prophet after me, it would be Umar.' After listing these, he concludes: 'So why did you not affirm the textual designation for them both?' The implication is that these statements are clear enough to be considered textual evidence for the succession of Abu Bakr and Umar, and the opponents' rejection is inconsistent.

Key Terms
نصّ
خلافة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That these hadith are merely about virtue and do not constitute explicit textual designation for the caliphate.
Correction: The author argues they are indeed nass, as they explicitly point to Abu Bakr's leadership and the Prophet's intent.

Checkpoint

B) To argue that these statements constitute explicit textual evidence (nass) for Abu Bakr's caliphate.
C) To prove that the Prophet never designated anyone.
D) To demonstrate that Umar was not worthy of the caliphate.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet ﷺ left multiple explicit statements that together provide strong textual basis for Abu Bakr's caliphate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you willing to submit to the explicit commands of the Prophet ﷺ regarding leadership, even if your personal inclinations or political views differ? Take one hadith from this passage and ask yourself: Do I truly believe in its implication for the caliphate, or do I rationalize it away?
?
The opponents are challenged for not inferring the proof from clear evidence. In your own life, how often do you ignore clear textual evidence in matters of creed or practice because it conflicts with your desires? What one thing from this passage will you stop ignoring today?
?
The Prophet ﷺ left clear statements about the caliphate, yet many then and now reject them. What does this tell you about your own readiness to accept the truth even when it is uncomfortable? Write down one hadith from this passage and commit to acting on it.

Hadith evidence for the virtue of Abu Bakr and Umar and the argument for nass
Baqlani lists hadith about Abu Bakr and Umar and asks why nass is not claimed for them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Baqlani uses hadith about Abu Bakr and Umar to challenge the Shia claim of explicit designation (nass) for Ali.

Core Idea
Baqlani turns the Shia's own evidence against them.

Imam Baqlani presents a series of hadith that highlight the virtues and leadership of Abu Bakr and Umar, which the Shia might consider as evidence for nass. He then poses a rhetorical challenge: if the Shia use such reports to claim nass for Ali, why not apply the same reasoning to Abu Bakr and Umar? This lesson explores Baqlani's logical move to expose inconsistency.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and list the hadith
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then go through the translation and note each hadith cited by Baqlani.
There are about 12 hadith in this passage.
2
Identify the common thread
Notice that each hadith praises Abu Bakr and/or Umar or indicates their leadership. Look for themes like merit, command, and prophethood-like qualities.
For example, the hadith about Umar being inspired by truth.
3
Understand the Shia claim for nass
Recall that Shia argue that certain hadith point to explicit designation (nass) of Ali as successor. Baqlani is using a similar style of argumentation.
The Shia rely on hadith like Ghadir Khumm.
4
Grasp Baqlani's rhetorical question
Baqlani asks: if you consider these hadith as evidence for nass for Ali, why do you not say nass for Abu Bakr and Umar based on these similar reports? This is meant to expose inconsistency.
The question is at the end of the passage: 'فكيف لم تقولوا بالنص عليهما؟'

وقوله : «لا ينبغي لقوم يكون فيهم أبو بكر أن يتقدمهم غيره» (١)، وقوله: «إيتوني بدواة وكتف أكتب لأبي بكر كتاباً لا يختلف عليه اثنان» (٢)، وقوله صلى الله عليه: «أنتما من الدين بمنزلة السمع والبصر من الرأس» (٣) ، وقوله : «لو كنت متخذاً خليلاً لاتخذت أبا بكر خليلاً ولكن صاحبكم خليل الرحمن» (٤) ، وقوله : «إن تولوها أبا بكر تجدوه ضعيفاً في بدنه قوياً في أمر الله وإن تولوها عمر تجدوه قوياً في بدنه قوياً في أمر الله وإن تولوها علياً تجدوه هادياً مهدياً» وعلموا بهذه البنية والترتيب أنه قصد التنبيه على النص عليه، وبقوله : «الخلافة بعدي إلى ثلاثين» (٥) ، وقوله : «إن يطع الناس أبا بكر وعمر رشدوا ورشدت أمتهم وإن يعصوهما غووا وغوت أمتهم» (٦) ، وقوله : «خير أمتي أبو بكر ثم عمر» (٧) ، وقوله : «من أفضل من أبي بكر؟ زوجني ابنته وجهزني بماله وجاهد معي ساعة الخوف» (٨) ، وقوله في عمر: «لو كان بعدي نبي لكان عمر» (٩) ، و«لو لم أُبعث فيكم لبعث عمر» (١٠) ، و«إن الله ضرب بالحق على لسان عمر وقلبه يقول الحق وإن كان مراً» (١١) ، و«إن منكم لمحدثين ومكلمين وإن عمر منهم» (١٢) ، في نظائر هذه الأخبار والفضائل التي يطول تتبعها ؛ فكيف لم تقولوا بالنص عليهما؟
And his saying: 'It is not befitting for a people among whom is Abu Bakr that anyone else should lead them' (1), and his saying: 'Bring me an inkpot and a shoulder blade so that I may write for Abu Bakr a document about which two would not differ' (2), and his saying, peace be upon him: 'You two (Abu Bakr and Umar) are to the religion as hearing and sight are to the head' (3), and his saying: 'If I were to take a close friend, I would have taken Abu Bakr as a close friend, but your companion is the Friend of the Merciful' (4), and his saying: 'If you entrust it (the caliphate) to Abu Bakr, you will find him weak in his body but strong in the matter of Allah; and if you entrust it to Umar, you will find him strong in his body and strong in the matter of Allah; and if you entrust it to Ali, you will find him a guide and guided' – and they understood by this structure and arrangement that he intended to indicate (al-tanbīh) the nass upon him, and his saying: 'The caliphate after me is for thirty years' (5), and his saying: 'If the people obey Abu Bakr and Umar, they will be rightly guided and their community will be rightly guided; and if they disobey them, they will go astray and their community will go astray' (6), and his saying: 'The best of my ummah is Abu Bakr, then Umar' (7), and his saying: 'Who is more excellent than Abu Bakr? He married me to his daughter, equipped me with his wealth, and struggled with me in the hour of fear' (8), and his saying concerning Umar: 'If there were to be a prophet after me, it would be Umar' (9), and 'If I had not been sent among you, Umar would have been sent' (10), and 'Indeed Allah has set truth upon the tongue of Umar and his heart; he speaks the truth even if it be bitter' (11), and 'Indeed among you are those who are inspired (muḥaddathūn) and addressed (mukallamūn), and Umar is among them' (12) – and in similar such reports and virtues whose pursuit would be lengthy; so why do you not say the nass (explicit designation) for them (i.e., for Abu Bakr and Umar)?
Source pages p. 470

Commentary
This passage is a collection of hadith evidence presented by Baqlani to argue against the Shia claim of explicit designation (nass) for Ali. He cites numerous hadith praising Abu Bakr and Umar and indicating their leadership, including statements that Abu Bakr should lead, that the Prophet intended Abu Bakr as successor, and that obedience to Abu Bakr and Umar leads to guidance. The hadith also highlight Umar's virtues, such as being inspired by truth. Baqlani then asks rhetorically: if the Shia consider such hadith as evidence for nass for Ali, why do they not say nass for Abu Bakr and Umar based on these similar reports? This argument aims to show inconsistency in the Shia position.

Key Terms
النص
أبو بكر
عمر
علي
الخلفاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Baqlani is asserting that Abu Bakr and Umar were explicitly designated as caliphs by nass.
Correction: Baqlani does not claim nass for Abu Bakr and Umar; he uses these hadith to argue that if the Shia consider similar reports as evidence for nass for Ali, consistency would require them to claim nass for Abu Bakr and Umar as well.

Checkpoint
What is the main purpose of Baqlani listing these hadith about Abu Bakr and Umar?
A) To prove that Abu Bakr and Umar were explicitly designated as caliphs by nass.
B) To argue that if the Shia claim nass for Ali based on similar hadith, they should also claim nass for Abu Bakr and Umar.
C) To show that Abu Bakr and Umar were superior to Ali.
D) To establish that the caliphate belongs only to the Quraysh.

Key Takeaway
Baqlani uses hadith about Abu Bakr and Umar to challenge the Shia by showing that if they consider such reports as evidence for nass for Ali, consistency requires them to claim nass for Abu Bakr and Umar as well.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are there areas in your life where you demand evidence for something from others but fail to apply the same standard to yourself? This lesson shows how inconsistency can undermine a position. Consider a belief you hold strongly: do you apply the same criteria to it as you do to opposing views? What would it take for you to be truly consistent?
?
Baqlani uses the Shia's own hadith to challenge them. When you argue with someone, do you seek to understand their evidence and then point out inconsistency, or do you simply dismiss them? How can you train yourself to argue more effectively by using their own sources against misconceptions?
?
The Shia claim nass for Ali based on certain hadith; Baqlani shows similar hadith for Abu Bakr and Umar. Are you willing to accept that your own sources might be interpreted differently if you apply a consistent method? This lesson challenges you to be honest about your hermeneutical principles. What is one area where you might be applying double standards in reading religious texts?

Refuting the Ahad Objection with Consistency
Baqlani refutes the ahad objection by demanding consistency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqlani uses the principle of consistency to refute the objection that the hadith about Abu Bakr and Umar are unreliable because they are solitary (ahad).

Core Idea
Consistency demands: the same standard must apply to both Sunni and Shia reports.

This passage captures Baqlani's sharp response to the Shia claim that the Sunni hadith about the virtues of Abu Bakr and Umar are ahad (solitary) and therefore unreliable. Instead of defending the transmission, Baqlani turns the argument around: if ahad reports are rejected, the same fate awaits the Shia's own traditions. He then exposes the opponent's double standard, accusing them of demanding blind acceptance of their own narratives while dismissing clear prophetic statements as dissimulation (taqiyya).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Note the structure: the objection from the opponent, then Baqlani's response beginning with 'it is said to them.'
Pay attention to the rhetorical question Baqlani poses.
2
Identify the two parts of the refutation
First, Baqlani points out that the same objection (ahad) applies to the Shia's own reports. Second, he accuses them of demanding Sunnis accept all Shia reports while reinterpreting clear texts as taqiyya.
3
Reflect on the principle of consistency
Consider why consistency in evaluating evidence is important in theological arguments. How does this strengthen Baqlani's position?
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا : كل هذه الأخبار آحاد غير ثابتة قيل لهم : فما الذي يمنع خصومكم على هذه الدعوى في أخباركم؟ فلا يجدون فصلاً . ثم يقال لهم : فكأنكم قد عزمتم على إنكار جميع ما نرويه لكم وتكذيبه ومطالبتنا بالإقرار والإذعان لجميع ما تروونه ؛ وكأنكم إنما تقولون لنا : سلموا لنا مذهبنا واتركوا الظاهر المعلوم من قول النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في أبي بكر وعمر وقول علي فيهما واحملوا ذلك على التقية منه وهذا من حديث النفوس وما لا سبيل لكم إلى المصير إليه.
If they say: 'All these reports are solitary (āḥād) and not established,' it is said to them: 'What prevents your opponents from the same claim regarding your reports?' Then they will find no distinction. Then it is said to them: 'It is as if you have resolved to deny all that we narrate to you and to declare it false, while demanding from us acceptance and submission to all that you narrate; and as if you are saying to us: "Submit to our madhhab and abandon the apparent, known statement of the Prophet, peace be upon him, concerning Abu Bakr and Umar, and the statement of Ali concerning them, and interpret that as taqiyya (dissimulation) from him" — and this is from the speech of souls, and there is no way for you to reach it.'
Source pages p. 471

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its answer. The opponent argues that the hadith cited by Baqlani are ahad (transmitted by a single chain) and therefore not reliable. Baqlani responds by turning the argument around: the same objection would apply to the Shia's own reports, so the opponent has no special basis to reject Sunni reports while accepting their own. He further accuses the opponent of bias, demanding that Sunnis accept all Shia narratives while dismissing Sunni ones. The opponent is also accused of asking to reinterpret clear statements of the Prophet and Ali about Abu Bakr and Umar as taqiyya (dissimulation), which Baqlani dismisses as baseless psychological speculation.

Key Terms
آحاد
التقية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ahad hadith are automatically invalid in all theological discussions.
Correction: The issue is not the inherent invalidity of ahad reports, but the need for consistent standards. Baqlani does not argue that ahad are valid; he argues that if ahad are rejected, the opponent's own traditions must also be rejected.

Checkpoint
How does Baqlani refute the objection that the hadith about Abu Bakr and Umar are ahad and unreliable?
A) He proves that these hadith are mutawatir.
B) He argues that the Shia's own reports are also ahad, so the objection is inconsistent.
C) He concedes the point and shifts to a different argument.
D) He says that ahad reports are sufficient for matters of imamate.

Key Takeaway
Baqlani refutes the ahad objection by demanding consistency: if ahad reports are rejected, the same standard must apply to the opponent's own traditions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a disagreement you've had where you held one standard for yourself and a different one for the other person. How does this passage expose the inconsistency in that kind of thinking? Are you willing to apply the same standard to both sides, even if it means admitting you were wrong?
?
Baqlānī accuses the opponent of demanding submission to their narratives while rejecting the other's. Where in your own life might you be demanding that others accept your perspective without giving them the same courtesy? What would it cost you to be truly consistent?
?
The opponent is asked to abandon the 'apparent, known statement' of the Prophet and reinterpret it as taqiyya. When have you twisted a clear truth to fit your preferred narrative? What would it take for you to accept the clear truth even when it contradicts your desires?

Establishing the imamate through choice (ikhtiyār) after nass is invalid
Baqlani explains that imamate is established by contract of ahl al-ḥall wa al-ʿaqd, not nass.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that when nass (explicit designation) is invalid, the imamate is established through contract by ahl al-ḥall wa al-ʿaqd, which is the method of choice (ikhtiyār).

Core Idea
Imamate is established by choice of the community, not by divine appointment alone.

After arguing against the validity of nass for a specific imam, Baqlani addresses the natural follow-up question: if not by nass, then how? In this passage, he lays out the Sunni position that the imamate is established by a contract from the people of loosening and binding (ahl al-ḥall wa al-ʿaqd), which is the method of choice. He also provides a logical proof for why choice is necessary once nass is invalidated.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice the question-and-answer format.
The passage is a direct response to an imagined objection.
2
Identify Baqlani's answer
Find the key phrase: 'إنما يصير الإمام إماماً بعقد من يعقد له الإمامة من أفاضل المسلمين الذين هم من أهل الحل والعقد'. This is the core positive claim.
Note that the contract is made by the virtuous Muslims, not just anyone.
3
Follow the logical proof
Baqlani argues that the only two ways to establish imamate are nass and choice. Since nass is invalid (as established earlier), choice must be valid. This is an argument by elimination.
The proof is concise: 'لأنه ليس لها طريق إلا النص أو الاختيار وفي فساد النص دليل على ثبوت الاختيار'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا : فإذا فسد النص على إمام بعينه فكيف طريق إثبات الإمامة وبماذا يصير الإمام إماماً؟ قيل لهم : إنما يصير الإمام إماماً بعقد من يعقد له الإمامة من أفاضل المسلمين الذين هم من أهل الحل والعقد والمؤتمنين على هذا الشأن لأنه ليس لها طريق إلا النص أو الاختيار وفي فساد النص دليل على ثبوت الاختيار الذي نذهب إليه.
If they say: 'If the nass (explicit designation) for a specific imam is invalid, then what is the way to establish the imamate, and by what does a person become an imam?' It is said to them: 'A person becomes an imam only by a contract (ʿaqd) from those who contract the imamate for him from among the virtuous Muslims who are the people of loosening and binding (ahl al-ḥall wa al-ʿaqd) and who are entrusted with this matter. Because there is no way to it except nass or choice (ikhtiyār). And the invalidity of nass is evidence for the establishment of the choice which we hold.'
Source pages p. 471

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof. Baqlani states the method of establishing the imamate after having shown that nass for a specific person is invalid. The questioner asks: if nass is invalid, how is imamate proven and how does one become imam? Baqlani answers that imamate is established by a contract made by the virtuous Muslims who are the people of loosening and binding (ahl al-ḥall wa al-ʿaqd). This is because the only possible methods are either explicit designation (nass) or election/choice (ikhtiyār). Since nass is invalid (as argued earlier), that very invalidity serves as evidence for the validity of choice, which is the Sunni position.

Key Terms
النص
الاختيار
أهل الحل والعقد
الإمامة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the invalidity of nass automatically proves choice without further reasoning.
Correction: Baqlani's argument relies on the premise that the only two possible methods are nass and choice; eliminating one necessarily establishes the other. Without that premise, invalidity of nass does not automatically prove choice.

Checkpoint
According to Baqlani, what is the only way to establish the imamate besides nass?
A) Hereditary succession
B) Majority vote of all Muslims
C) Contract by ahl al-ḥall wa al-ʿaqd
D) Divine appointment

Key Takeaway
The only way to establish imamate after nass is invalid is through contract by ahl al-ḥall wa al-ʿaqd, which is the method of choice (ikhtiyār).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you assume that leadership in your community must come from a direct divine appointment, or do you accept the responsibility of choosing qualified leaders? How does Baqlani's argument challenge you to take your role in communal decisions more seriously? Will you start actively participating in the selection of leaders, even in small settings?
?
The passage describes the contracting group as 'the virtuous Muslims who are entrusted with this matter.' Are you striving to be among those who are qualified and trusted? If not, what specific steps will you take to become more knowledgeable and trustworthy in matters affecting the Muslim community?

The Sufficiency of One Person for the Contract of Imamate
Baqlani states that one person suffices for the contract of imamate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqlani's argument that the imamate can be contracted by a single qualified person and the evidence from the absence of a specified number.

Core Idea
One qualified person suffices to appoint an imam.

In this passage, Baqlani addresses a key question about the minimum number required to establish an imam. He argues that a single qualified individual from the people of loosening and binding is sufficient, and supports this with a principled argument from silence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its English translation. Notice the question-and-answer format.
The passage is a dialogue between an objector and Baqlani.
2
Identify the question and answer
The first question asks about the number needed for the contract. The answer is 'one man from ahl al-ḥall wa al-ʿaqd'.
3
Understand the evidence from absence
When asked for evidence, Baqlani argues that since no specific number is required by revelation or reason, the default is that one is sufficient.
This is an argument from the lack of evidence for a minimum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال قائل : فبكم يتم عقد الإمامة عندكم؟ قيل له : تنعقد وتتم برجل واحد من أهل الحل والعقد إذا عقدها لرجل على صفة ما يجب أن يكون عليه الأئمة فإن قالوا وما الدليل على ذلك؟ قيل لهم : الدليل عليه أنه إذا صح أن فضلاء الأمة هم ولاة عقد الإمامة ولم يقم دليل على أنه يجب أن يعقدها سائرها ولا عدد منهم مخصوص لا تجوز الزيادة عليه والنقصان منه ثبت بفقد الدليل على تعيين العدد والعلم بأنه ليس بموجود في الشريعة ولا في أدلة العقول أنها تنعقد بالواحِدِ فما فوقه.
If someone says: 'By what number is the contract of imamate completed according to you?' It is said to him: 'It is contracted and completed by one man from the people of loosening and binding if he contracts it for a man who possesses the qualities that an imam must have.' If they say: 'And what is the evidence for that?' It is said to them: 'The evidence for it is that if it is established that the virtuous of the ummah are the authorities for contracting the imamate, and there is no evidence that the entirety of them must contract it, nor a specific number from them that cannot be increased or decreased, then it is established by the lack of evidence specifying the number, and by the knowledge that it is not found in the Shariah nor in the proofs of intellects that it is contracted by one and above.'
Source pages p. 471

Commentary
This passage defines the minimum number required for the contract of imamate according to Sunni doctrine. Baqlani states that the contract is valid with one qualified person from ahl al-ḥall wa al-ʿaqd, provided that the candidate possesses the necessary qualifications. When asked for evidence, he argues using a principle of absence: since it is established that the virtuous Muslims are the authorities for this contract, and there is no textual or rational evidence requiring a specific number (e.g., a quorum), the default is that even one person suffices. The lack of evidence for a minimum number proves that the number is not restricted, so one is enough.

Key Terms
أهل الحل والعقد
عقد الإمامة
العدد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many think that the contract of imamate requires consensus or a large group of representatives.
Correction: Baqlani demonstrates that the burden of proof is on those who claim a specific number; in its absence, one qualified person is sufficient.

Checkpoint
What is the minimum number of people from ahl al-ḥall wa al-ʿaqd needed to contract the imamate according to Baqlani?
A) Two witnesses
B) Three elders
C) One person
D) Forty scholars

Key Takeaway
The imamate can be validly contracted by a single qualified person from ahl al-ḥall wa al-ʿaqd.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a clear proof from the Quran or Sunnah, do you ever hesitate to follow it because not enough people around you practice it? What is holding you back?
?
Consider a recent decision you made that affected others. Did you seek the opinion of one qualified person or did you demand multiple opinions to feel safe? How does Baqlani's argument challenge your approach?
?
Are you among the 'people of loosening and binding' in your community? If so, are you fulfilling your responsibility to appoint righteous leaders? If not, how can you encourage those who do?
